Abidjan is a district of Côte d'Ivoire located in the Ivory Coast, serving as the country's largest city. This major urban center covers a total area of 2,119 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 18 meters above sea level. With a substantial population of 6,321,017 residents, the inhabitants of Abidjan are known as Abidjanais. The district operates under the motto "District d'Abidjan, acteur de développement" and uses the area code +225. Abidjan follows GMT time zone with a UTC offset of +0. The city holds significant administrative importance, serving as the capital of Crime in Ivory Coast, the Lagunes Region, and the Sud Department. Beyond its role as Ivory Coast's largest city, Abidjan also functions as the largest city for Crime in Ivory Coast and is notably located within Sub-Saharan Africa. Abidjan houses several important institutions and landmarks. The Parliament of Ivory Coast, Culture Palace of Abidjan, and Village Ivoire are all located within the city. Educational institutions include the University of Science and Technology of Ivory Coast and CIFAD, which maintains a campus there. The city has also hosted significant sporting events, including the 1984 African Cup of Nations Final and the 2009 African Nations Championship Final. The city serves as headquarters for multiple organizations, including the Democratic Party of Ivory Coast – African Democratic Rally, Incubateur Régional d'Afrique de l'Ouest, and Interivoire. Universal Music Africa has its location city in Abidjan. Several sports clubs call Abidjan their ground, including JC d'Abidjan, Stade d'Abidjan, and Stella Club d'Adjamé. The Ivorian Republican Guard maintains its garrison in the city. Abidjan has been the birthplace of notable individuals including Priscille Kreto, Robert Sankara, and Roger Aholou. The city has also been the final resting place for Robert Guéï, Christian Bonaud, and Christian Lattier. In the entertainment sphere, musical groups Magic System and rapper Ak47 consider Abidjan their hometown, while Marcel Blaguet Ledjou has his occupation based in the city.
Addis Ababa, the capital city of Ethiopia and one of its regions, serves as a major urban center with a total area of 527.0 square kilometers and a land area of 527,000,000 square meters. The city was founded by Menelik II and Taytu Betul and sits at an elevation of 2,354.8848 meters above sea level. With a total population of 2,739,551 residents, Addis Ababa has a population density of 5,165.1 people per square kilometer. The inhabitants of the city are known as Addis Ababans, and the area code is (+251) 11. The city operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3. Throughout its history, Addis Ababa has served as the capital for multiple Ethiopian governments, including the Derg, the People's Democratic Republic of Ethiopia, and the Transitional Government of Ethiopia. The city has been the site of significant historical events, including the Battle of Segale, the 1960 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt, and the 1989 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt. The city is home to numerous educational institutions, including Menelik II School, Unity University (which has both its campus and main city location there), and Royal College, Addis Abeba. Several notable individuals were born in Addis Ababa, including Rophnan, Sayat Demissie, and Meron Getnet, while others such as Caleb Meakins, Belay Zeleke, and Dawit Nega died there. Hizkias Assefa received his education in the city. Addis Ababa serves as a significant economic and commercial hub, housing the headquarters of major organizations such as the Prosperity Party, Development Bank of Ethiopia, and United Ethiopian Democratic Forces. The Commercial Bank of Ethiopia Headquarters is located in the city, along with financial institutions like Enat Bank and the Metals and Engineering Corporation. Several prominent residents include Oumer Hussein, Ahmed Shide, and Abune Mathias. The city has a strong military presence, with various units maintaining garrisons there, including Mehal Sefari, the 65th Infantry Division "Granatieri di Savoia," and Kebur Zabagna. Sports teams such as Defence Force S.C., Ethio Electric S.C., and Saint George S.C. use Addis Ababa as their home ground. Cultural life flourishes in the city, with musical groups like Endegna, Walias Band, and Getatchew Mekurya calling it their hometown. The television series Betoch is set in Addis Ababa, and the Dembel City Center is located there. The city also serves as an assembly location for vehicles, including the Tofaş Şahin and Hyundai Ioniq. Addis Ababa is considered part of Sub-Saharan Africa, reflecting its important position within the broader African continent.
Adelaide is a major Australian city with a total population of 1,387,290. The city serves as the location for several notable establishments and productions, including Castle Plaza, Prescott Schools, and the television series Sam Fox: Extreme Adventures. Adelaide has been the birthplace of several prominent individuals across different fields. In the world of cricket, Cameron Williams was born in the city, while the arts have been represented by natives Carl Tietjens and Carlee Taylor, both of whom were also born there. The city has also served as the final resting place for notable figures from various backgrounds. Carl Linger, Pāvils Dreijmanis, and Quentin Kenihan all passed away in Adelaide, marking the city as significant in both the beginnings and endings of these individuals' lives.
Ahmedabad is a metropolis located in India that serves as a major urban center with significant geographical, administrative, and cultural importance. The city covers a total area of 505 square kilometers, while its urban area spans an impressive 1.866 billion square meters. Situated at an elevation of 53 meters above sea level, Ahmedabad has a total population of 8,253,000 residents, who are known by the demonyms Ahmedabadi or Amdavadi. The city operates under a mayor-council government system and is administered by the Amdavad Municipal Corporation as its governing body. Ahmedabad uses the area code 079 for telecommunications and the postal code format 380 0XX for mail services. The city follows Indian Standard Time with a UTC offset of +5:30. Ahmedabad holds considerable historical significance, having served as the capital of both the Gujarat Sultanate and Gujarat under the Mughal Empire. The city is home to several notable landmarks and institutions, including the Calico Dome, Sanskar Kendra, and Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel International Airport, which serves as the city's primary aviation hub. The metropolis has produced numerous notable individuals across various fields. Amit Dave, Pradipsinh Jadeja, and Priti Sengupta were all born in Ahmedabad, while the city also served as the final resting place for Prahalad Chunnilal Vaidya, Pranlal Kharsani, and Pransukh Nayak. Several prominent figures have educational connections to the city, including Nikhil Paramjit Sharma, Disha Vakani, and Sheba Chhachhi, while others like Pradip Parmar, Rengaswamy Ramesh, and Mavji Desai have made Ahmedabad their place of residence. The city serves as an important industrial and manufacturing center, with several Suzuki vehicle models being assembled there, including the Baleno subcompact, the third-generation Dzire, and the sixth-generation Swift. Major corporations have established their presence in Ahmedabad, with Adani Ports & SEZ and Calico Mills (Ahmedabad Manufacturing and Calico Printing Mills) having their location city there. Ahmedabad's educational landscape includes institutions such as the Entrepreneurship Development Institute of India, Smt. NHL Municipal Medical College, and Care Institute of Medical Sciences. The healthcare sector is represented by facilities like SVP Hospital and Ahmedabad Civil Hospital, both located in the region. The city's cultural and entertainment scene is enriched by organizations and groups with local connections. Bochasanwasi Akshar Purushottam Swaminarayan Sanstha, DD Girnar, and Colors Gujarati all have their headquarters in Ahmedabad, while musical acts like Meghdhanush band, Mauli Dave, and the duo Shyamal-Saumil call the city their hometown. The Gujarat Titans cricket team uses Ahmedabad as their ground for matches. Military presence in the city is maintained by the 11th Indian Infantry Division, which has its garrison stationed in Ahmedabad. The city's transportation infrastructure includes the Ahmedabad Municipal Transport Service, which serves the region, along with ride-sharing services like MylesCar that operate in the area. The food service industry is represented by Jasuben Pizza, which serves the Ahmedabad region. Natural attractions near the city include Vastrapur Lake, Indian Wild Ass Sanctuary, and Kankaria Lake, all of which have Ahmedabad as their nearest city. The Gujarat Metro Rail Corporation Limited has historical connections to Ahmedabad as its predecessor organization.
Algiers, the capital city of Algeria, is a major metropolitan center with a total area of 363 square kilometers and a metropolitan area spanning 1,190,000,000 square meters. The city has a total population of 4,510,000 residents, resulting in a population density of 12,424 people per square kilometer, while the metropolitan area maintains a density of 7,012 people per square kilometer. Algiers operates in the Central European Time zone with a UTC offset of +01:00, and its postal codes range from 16000 to 16132. The city's area code is (+213) 021. The city serves as home to numerous educational and cultural institutions, including the Roma Italian School of Algiers, the University of Science and Technology Houari Boumediene, and the National Polytechnic School. The Botanical Garden Hamma provides a natural retreat within the urban landscape, while various government bodies such as the Electricity and Gas Regulation Commission and the Supreme Council of the Arabic language in Algeria maintain their operations there. Algiers has been the site of significant historical events, including the Capture of Peñón of Algiers in 1529, the Battle of Algiers from 1956 to 1957, and the Battle of Bab El Oued. The city has served as the capital for multiple political entities throughout history, including French Algeria, the Provisional Government of the French Republic, and the Provisional Government of the Algerian Republic. Several notable individuals have connections to Algiers through birth, death, or residence. Roger Hanin, Samira Negrouche, and Baya El Hachemi were all born in the city, while Saïd Bouhadja, Léon Carré, and Léon Cauvy died there. Contemporary residents include Adam Larfi and Inès Ibbou, and the city serves as the hometown for Amel Brahim-Djelloul, Biyouna, and Julie Pietri. The city's cultural significance extends to music, as Algiers is recognized as the stylistic origin of Sanaa music. Various media organizations, including Samira TV, the Public Establishment of Television, and Algeria Press Service, have established their headquarters or operations in the city. Political organizations such as the Democratic National Rally and the Canary Islands Independence Movement also maintain headquarters there. Algiers serves as a military center, hosting garrisons for the Commodore-in-Charge Algiers, the Republican Guard, and the Algerian Land Forces. The city has been a venue for multiple Algerian Cup Finals, including those held in 2010, 2011, and 2012, and serves as the ground for various football clubs including NA Hussein Dey and teams from the 1939-40 USM Alger season and 2011-12 USM El Harrach season. The city's industrial significance is demonstrated by its role as an assembly location for the Renault Dauphine. Algiers is situated near the Mediterranean Sea and is associated with regional cuisine, particularly Tajine Mtewem. The city has also attracted international architectural attention, with John McAslan having designed significant buildings there. Additionally, Henry Stanyford Blanckley's occupation is connected to Algiers, and Jean-Baptiste Nouvion has spousal connections to the city.
Almaty is a major city in Kazakhstan, serving as the country's largest city and formerly the capital of the Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic. The city covers a total area of 682.0 square kilometers, while its metropolitan area spans an impressive 9,395,000,000.0 square meters. With a total population of 1,977,011 residents, Almaty operates under the governance of the Almaty City Mäslihat and uses postal codes ranging from 050000 to 050063. The city's telecommunications are served by the area code +7 727, and it operates in the UTC+6 time zone with a UTC offset of +6. Almaty is home to numerous notable landmarks and institutions. The President's Residence, Satbayev Memorial Museum, and Sayran Lake are all located within the city. The Satbayev University and Qazaq Radiosy also operate from Almaty, while the city hosted the 2013 Asian Shotgun Championships. Several natural attractions lie near the city, including Big Almaty Lake, Shymbulak, and Charyn National Park, all of which list Almaty as their nearest city. The city has significant connections to various notable individuals. Roman Chentsov, Roman Kirsch, and Sanzhar Mustafin were all born in Almaty, while Boris Blinov, Boris Katalymov, and Uzakbay Karamanov died there. Several prominent figures maintain residences in the city, including tennis player Zarina Diyas, Timur Khabibulin, and Aleksandr Nedovyesov. Additionally, Holy Dragons, Liza Umarova, and Deniz Reno all consider Almaty their hometown. The city is also associated with Yesken Sergebayev's notable work and was the site of the historical event Jeltoqsan. Almaty serves as a hub for various organizations and businesses. Multiple airlines operate from the city, with Bek Air using it as a target airport. The city houses the headquarters of Prime Aviation, Rukhaniyat Party, and Democratic Party Adilet. Several sports teams call Almaty home, including AFC Kairat, FC Alma-Ata, and FC Megasport, all of which use the city as their ground. The Almaty Arena operates within the city as well. The city maintains a strong military presence, serving as a garrison for the Central Asian Military District, Central Military Band of the Ministry of Defense of Kazakhstan, and Internal Troops of Kazakhstan. Almaty's industrial sector includes the assembly of Hyundai H350 vehicles. The city encompasses various districts and areas, including Medeu District and Akbulak, Kazakhstan, both classified as types within Almaty. The 2021 Almaty City Mäslihat election took place in the country, reflecting the city's ongoing political significance in Kazakhstan.

The city's residents are known as Ammanis, and the area operates under the postal code range 11110-17198, with the area code +962(6) and a UTC offset of +3. As Jordan's capital, Amman has historically served as the capital for several political entities, including the former Emirate of Transjordan and during the Jordanian annexation of the West Bank. The city has been the site of significant military engagements, including the Battle of Nablus in 1918, the First Battle of Amman, and the First Battle of the Jordan, with notable military figures such as Zubayr ibn al-Awwam and Henri Vanwaetermeulen participating in battles there. Amman hosts numerous organizations and institutions across various sectors. The city serves as the location for Campbell Gray Living, the Amman Center for Human Rights Studies, and the Amman Stand-up Comedy Festival. Several companies have established their headquarters in Amman, including the American Center of Research, Ammon News, and Roya TV. The city is also home to investment and technology firms such as Zara Investment Holding, Jobedu, and Tamatem Games. The educational landscape includes institutions like Princess Sumaya University for Technology and the National Orthodox School, both located in the city. Nasser Judeh received his education in Amman. The city's transportation infrastructure includes Queen Alia International Airport, which serves as a target airport for DHL International Aviation ME. Amman's healthcare sector features several prominent medical facilities, including Jordan Hospital, Specialty Hospital Jordan, Prince Hamza Hospital, Arab Medical Center, and King Hussein Cancer Center, all operating within the city or region. The military presence is significant, with the Royal Jordanian Air Force, Royal Jordanian Army, and 3rd Armored Division maintaining garrisons in Amman. The city has cultural significance as the hometown of several musical groups, including JadaL, El Morabba3, and Akher Zapheer. Amman has been the birthplace of notable individuals such as Rouzbahan Fraij, Sama'a Khraisat, and Sami al-Oraydi, while also serving as the final resting place for Behnam Abu Alsoof, Samir Al-Rifai, and Samir Ghawshah. Amsterdam, the capital of the Netherlands, is a municipality with a total population of 907,976 residents, who are known as Amsterdammers. The city covers a total area of 219.32 square kilometers, comprising 165,760,000 square meters of land and 53,560,000 square meters of water. Located at an elevation of -2.0 meters below sea level, Amsterdam operates under the motto "Heldhaftig, Vastberaden, Barmhartig" (Valiant, Steadfast, Compassionate). The city is governed by a municipal council and uses the area code 020, with postal codes ranging from 1000 to 1183. Amsterdam operates in two time zones: Central European Time and Central European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2 respectively. Amsterdam serves as the location for several notable institutions and landmarks, including the Amsterdam Museum, the Press Museum, and Prins Hendrikkade. The city has been the site of significant historical events, including the Bijltjesoproer, the Anabaptist riot, and Operation Ramrod 16. The city has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Calvin Jong-a-Pin, Calvin Mac-Intosch, and Calvin Valies. Amsterdam has also served as the final resting place for prominent figures such as Cab Kaye, Caesar ten Cate, and Carel Victor Gerritsen, who all died in the city.
Ankara, the capital city of Turkey and one of the country's metropolitan municipalities, was founded by Mustafa Kemal Atatürk. Located at an elevation of 938 meters, the city covers a total area of 24,521 square kilometers with an urban area spanning 2,767,850,000 square meters. The metropolitan area has a population density of 234 people per square kilometer, while the total population reaches 5,747,325 residents, who are known as Ankarans. The city operates under area code 1 and postal code 06xxx, following Turkey's time zone with a UTC offset of +3. As Turkey's capital, Ankara serves as the seat of government for the Grand National Assembly and was historically the capital of the Ankara Eyalet. The city houses numerous important government institutions, including the Ministry of Culture and Tourism of Turkey, the Capital Markets Board of Turkey, and the Presidential Complex. The General Staff of the Turkish Armed Forces maintains its garrison in Ankara, alongside the Gendarmerie Special Operations and Gendarmerie Search and Rescue Battalion Command. Ankara's significance extends beyond its political role, as it hosts several major educational institutions. Ankara University Faculty of Veterinary Medicine operates within the state, while Başkent University and Ankara Yıldırım Beyazıt University have established their campuses in the city. The Roman Baths of Ankara stand as a testament to the city's historical importance, and the area has witnessed significant historical events including the Battle of Ancyra, the Siege of Ankara, and the 1962 Turkish coup d'état attempt. The city serves as a major industrial and economic center, with Turkish Aerospace Industries, GAMA Enerji, and ASFAT establishing their operations there. Vehicle assembly also takes place in Ankara, where both the MAN Lion's City and Neoplan Skyliner are manufactured. Several sports clubs call Ankara home, including Bağlumspor, Sitespor, and Çubukspor, while the city hosted the 2012 Turkish Cup Final. Ankara has been the birthplace of notable figures such as Cahit Zarifoğlu, Can Dündar, and Cansu Dere, while also serving as the final resting place for Pınar Köksal, Samim Bilgen, and Sarkis Minassian. The city has been home to prominent architects Vedat Tek and Cengiz Bektaş, who created significant buildings there. Contemporary residents include Beytullah Kayışdağ, Sadık Savaş, and Salih Aydın, while musicians RockA, Nükleer Başlıklı Kız, and Benyamin Sönmez consider Ankara their hometown. The Progressive Republican Party of Turkey maintains its headquarters in the city, and Philip S. Kosnett has professional connections to Ankara. Additionally, Osman Kavala received his education in the city, and Dikmen Vadisi is located near Ankara.

The city operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3, and its area code is (+261) 023. As Madagascar's primary urban center, Antananarivo has served as the capital for multiple political entities throughout the country's history, including the Democratic Republic of Madagascar, French Madagascar, and the Third Republic of Madagascar. The city's significance extends beyond its current role, having been the seat of government across different historical periods. The city is also home to several educational institutions, including Institut Supérieur Polytechnique Arsenal, College of Saint Michael in Amparibe, and Saint Michael Higher Technical Institute in Amparibe. Antananarivo has been the site of significant historical events, including the 2006 Malagasy coup d'état attempt. The city continues to serve as a transportation hub, with Tsaradia airline designating it as a target airport for their operations.
Asmara serves as the capital city of Eritrea and stands as the country's largest city as well. This significant urban center is situated at an elevation of 2,325 meters and covers a total area of 45.0 square kilometers. The city supports a substantial population, with 963,000 residents within the city proper and a metropolitan area population of 1,258,001, resulting in a population density of 19,911 people per square kilometer. Asmara operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +03:00. The city has historically served as an important administrative center, functioning as the capital for Eritrea Province and Eritrea Governorate in addition to its current role as the national capital. Asmara hosts numerous significant institutions and organizations, including the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Eritrea, which maintains both its location and headquarters there. The Eritrean Telecommunications Corporation is also based in the city, along with the People's Front for Democracy and Justice, which has established its headquarters in Asmara. Additionally, the Alliance for the Re-liberation of Somalia operates its headquarters from the city. Educational institutions have a notable presence in Asmara, with the University of Asmara and the Istituto Italiano Statale Omnicomprensivo di Asmara both located within the city. The Eritrean Air Force maintains a garrison in Asmara, and several football clubs call the city home, including Denden FC, Dahlak SC, and Tesfa FC, all of which use Asmara as their ground. Asmara has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Sammy Habte, Biniam Girmay, and Dawit Isaak. The city has also been home to Ruth Abraha and Alex Kahsay. Conversely, it has served as the final resting place for Desiet Kidane, Abune Antonios, and Abune Phillipos. The city has witnessed significant historical events, including the 2013 Eritrean Army mutiny that took place there. In terms of aviation connections, DHL International Aviation ME designates Asmara as a target airport for its operations.
Astana serves as the capital city of Kazakhstan and operates under a mayor-council government system, with the Astana City Mäslihat functioning as its governing body. The city has a total population of 1,136,008 residents, while its metropolitan area encompasses 1,200,000 people across a total area of 810.2 square kilometers. Astana's strategic location makes it the nearest major city to important natural areas, including Buiratau National Park and Korgalzhyn Nature Reserve, highlighting its significance not only as an administrative center but also as a gateway to Kazakhstan's natural heritage.
Asunción, the capital city of Paraguay, serves as both the nation's capital and largest city. Founded on August 15, 1537, this historic city encompasses a total area of 117.0 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 42.9768 meters above sea level. The city maintains a population density of 4,411 people per square kilometer, with a total population of 525,252 residents within the city proper and a metropolitan population of 2,722,668 spread across a metropolitan area of 1,014,000,000 square meters. Residents of Asunción are known as Asuncenos, and the city operates under the postal code system 1001–1925 with the area code +595 (21). As a district of Paraguay, Asunción has historically served as the capital for various administrative entities, including the former Governorate of Paraguay, and continues to be recognized as the center of Paraguayan architecture. The city has been the site of numerous significant historical events, including the Sacking of Asunción, the 1989 Paraguayan coup d'état, and the 1996 Paraguayan coup d'état attempt. Several notable figures have connections to Asunción through birth or death, including Carlos Antonio López, who was both born and died in the city, Carlos Bonet, Camila Giangreco Campiz, Carmen Casco de Lara Castro, and Roberto Cabañas. Asunción serves as a cultural and linguistic center where the Maká language is spoken, and it houses important cultural institutions such as the Casa de la Independencia Museum. The city has hosted various sporting events, including the 2009 and 2010 Copa Petrobras Asunción tournaments and the 2022 Pan American Fencing Championships. Educational institutions flourish in Asunción, with Universidad Americana and Universidad Católica "Nuestra Señora de la Asunción" both located within the city. The sports scene is vibrant, with several football clubs calling Asunción home, including Deportivo Recoleta, Club Olimpia, and Club Oriental, all of which have their grounds in the city. Political activity centers in Asunción as well, with multiple parties maintaining their headquarters there, including the Progressive Democratic Party, Beloved Fatherland Party, and Patriotic Alliance for Change. The city has also nurtured musical talent, serving as the hometown for bands Ripe Banana Skins and Flou. Several prominent individuals have chosen Asunción as their place of residence, including tennis player Verónica Cepede Royg, athlete Leryn Franco, and Rossana de los Ríos. The city has also been recognized in awards, with Félix Toranzos receiving an award associated with Asunción. Additionally, Cateura is classified as a type of Asunción, further demonstrating the city's administrative and geographical significance within Paraguay.
Athens, the capital city of Greece, serves as a major metropolitan center with a total population of 637,798 residents, who are known as Athenians. The city encompasses a total area of 38.964 square kilometers, while its urban area extends across 412,000,000 square meters and the broader metropolitan area covers an impressive 2,928,717,000 square meters, housing a metropolitan population of 3,722,544 people. The city operates under a mayor-council government system and uses the area code 21 for telecommunications. Postal services are organized through codes following the patterns 10x xx, 11x xx, and 120 xx. Athens observes two time zones depending on the season: East European Time and Eastern European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +2 and +3 respectively. Athens holds significant historical and cultural importance, housing notable institutions such as the Benaki Museum. The city also features prominent accommodations like the President Hotel Athens and important governmental buildings including the Presidential Mansion, Athens. Throughout history, Athens has been the site of several significant events, including the Dekemvriana, the Battle of Piraeus, and the ancient Siege of Athens in 287 BC. The city has been home to various notable individuals throughout history. Quartus was both born and died in Athens, as did the singer Robert Williams. Roula Koromila was born in the city, while Beata Kitsikis died there, demonstrating Athens' continuing role as a significant center for prominent figures across different eras.

The city operates under the governance of the Auckland Council and uses the area code 09 for telephone services. Postal services are organized through codes ranging from 0600 to 2699. Auckland follows the time zone designated as Time in New Zealand, with UTC offsets of both +12:00 and +13:00 depending on seasonal adjustments. The city has also served as the birthplace for several individuals, including Caleb Olliff, Callan Mulvey, and Callum Hedge. Baghdad, the capital city and metropolis of Iraq, was founded by Al-Mansur on July 30, 762. This major urban center operates under a mayor-council government system and covers a total area of 673.0 square kilometers at an elevation of 34.0 meters above sea level. The city's residents are known as Baghdadis, and it uses postal codes ranging from 10001 to 10090, operating in the UTC+3 time zone. The city serves as a linguistic hub where both Mandaic language and Baghdadi Arabic are spoken. Baghdad has been the capital of several historical entities, including the Arab Federation, Mandatory Iraq, and the Coalition Provisional Authority. Its strategic importance is reflected in the various military installations located there, including Camp Cropper, Camp Liberty, and Camp Nama, which have served as garrisons for the United States Forces – Iraq, the Sixth Army of the Ottoman Empire, and the 6th Division of Iraq. Baghdad has been the site of significant historical events, including the Capture of Baghdad in 1624 and 1638, as well as the more recent Camp Liberty killings. The city has produced notable individuals across various fields, serving as the birthplace of Carmel Eliash, Amira Nur al-Din, and Qais Al-Sindy. It has also been the final resting place for several prominent figures, including Amira Nur al-Din, Qasim Mahmoud, and Qays Abd al-Hussein al-Yasiri. The city's cultural significance extends to the arts, with Jawad Saleem creating notable work there, while musicians Motez, Namir, and Simor Jalal call Baghdad their hometown. The city houses important educational institutions, including the College of Science – University of Baghdad and the University of Al-Ma'mun. Various organizations have established their headquarters in Baghdad, such as the Progress Party of Iraq, the Ministry of Planning of Iraq, and Journal Iraq. Baghdad's culinary traditions include regional specialties like Kubbeh and Masgouf. The city serves as a residence for political figures including Barham Salih and religious leaders such as Denha I and Sabrisho IV. Aviation connections include Jupiter Airlines and DHL International Aviation ME, both of which target Baghdad as a destination airport. The city has also served as a launch site for the Al-Abid project and hosts the 1986 Iraqi Perseverance Cup, while Al-Rasheed SC uses Baghdad as their ground. Additionally, the city is associated with the Tacuinum Sanitatis and has connections to historical figures like Ibn al-Tilmidh, who had occupational ties to Baghdad, and Al-Mustansir II, who had Baghdad as a predecessor. The Voice of Iraq and Hisham N. Ashkouri, who received a Baghdad award, further demonstrate the city's ongoing cultural and media significance.

Bamako, the capital and largest city of Mali, serves as the nation's political, economic, and cultural center. The city has a total population of 2,713,000 people within an area of 245 square kilometers, resulting in a population density of 7,384.11 people per square kilometer. The broader metropolitan area encompasses 17,141,610,000 square meters and houses 2,757,234 residents, with a metropolitan population density of 160.85 people per square kilometer. Located at an elevation of 350 meters above sea level, Bamako operates on UTC±00:00 time zone. The city's historical significance extends beyond its current role as Mali's capital, having previously served as the capital of both French Sudan and Upper Senegal and Niger during the colonial period. Bamako has witnessed significant political events, including the 1968 and 1991 Malian coups d'état that took place within the city. Several notable individuals have connections to Bamako through birth or death. Roger Antoine, Samba Ousemane Sow, and footballer Samba Sow (born 1989) were all born in the city, while Baréma Bocoum, Garan Fabou Kouyate, and Modibo Keita (born 1942) died there. The city is also the hometown of renowned musicians including Vieux Farka Touré, Trio Da Kali, and the duo Amadou & Mariam. Bamako's infrastructure includes several important facilities and institutions. Modibo Keita International Airport serves the city and is a target airport for Eagle Air (Guinea) and Sky Mali airlines. The Pavillon des Sports Modibo Keita provides sporting facilities, while the Sacred Heart Cathedral represents the city's religious architecture. Educational institutions include the University of Bamako and Mandé Bukari University, both located within the city. The city hosts various sports teams, with Djoliba AC, AS Real Bamako, and Atar Club all having their grounds in Bamako. The 2002 Africa Cup of Nations Final was held in the city, highlighting its importance as a sporting venue. Several organizations have established their headquarters in Bamako, including the Democratic Union of the Malian People, the United Nations Multidimensional Integrated Stabilization Mission in Mali, and Douniah Airlines. Additionally, Aéroports du Mali and Sotelma have their location cities in Bamako, contributing to the city's role as a business center. Bamako Sign Language is spoken within the city, reflecting its linguistic diversity. The nearby Badinko Faunal Reserve has Bamako as its nearest city, indicating the capital's proximity to important natural areas in the region.

Bogotá, the capital city of Colombia, stands as a major metropolitan center with a rich history and significant contemporary importance. Bogotá has served as the capital for multiple historical entities, including the Republic of New Granada and the United States of Colombia, in addition to its current role as Colombia's capital. The city encompasses a total area of 307.36 square kilometers, with its urban area spanning 1,587,000,000 square meters. Bogotá's population totals 8,034,649 residents, while the metropolitan area houses 12,772,828 people. Brasília, the federal capital of Brazil, stands as a remarkable planned city founded on April 21, 1960. Located at an elevation of 1,172 meters, the city encompasses a total area of 5,801.998125202735 square kilometers and maintains a population density of 480.827 people per square kilometer. The metropolitan area is home to 4,291,577 residents, who are known as Brasilienses. The city operates in the Time in Brazil zone with a UTC offset of −03:00, and its postal code system begins with 70000-000, while the area code is +55 61. Brasília's motto, expressed both in English as "To the coming winds" and in Latin as "Venturis ventis," reflects the city's forward-looking character. As the capital of Brazil, Brasília has served as the seat of government for the Fourth Brazilian Republic and continues in this role during the current period of Brazilian history from 1985 to the present. The city hosts numerous important institutions and organizations, including the Brazilian Air Force, Brazilian Army, and Brazilian Army General Staff, all of which maintain garrisons there.
