Chicago, founded on August 12, 1833, by Jean Baptiste Point du Sable, is a major municipality in Illinois with a rich history and significant demographic presence. The city operates under a mayor-council government system, with the Chicago City Council serving as its governing body. Chicago's motto reflects its character as "Urbs in Horto" (City in a Garden) and "I Will," embodying both its natural beauty and determined spirit. Geographically, Chicago covers a total area of 607.43 square kilometers, comprising 589,817,992.37 square meters of land and 17,611,919.15 square meters of water. The city sits at an elevation of 182.02 meters above sea level and maintains a population density of 4,656.33 people per square kilometer. With a total population of 2,746,388 residents, known as Chicagoans, the metropolitan area extends to encompass 9,618,502 people, making it one of the largest urban centers in the United States. The city's infrastructure is well-organized with postal codes ranging from 606xx to 608xx series, and telephone service provided through area codes 312/872 and 773/872. Chicago operates in both Central Standard Time and Central Daylight Time zones, with UTC offsets of −06:00 and −05:00 respectively. Chicago has served as the location for numerous significant organizations and institutions, including the American Association for Applied Linguistics and the American Society for Bioethics and Humanities. The city has also been the site of important historical events, such as the Battle of Fort Dearborn, the Aldermen's wars, and the Tong Wars. Additionally, Camp Douglas was located within the city during its operational period. The city has been home to many notable individuals throughout its history. Chicago served as the birthplace of several prominent figures, including Cal Lepore, Cam Collier, and Camille Yarbrough. The city has also been the final resting place for notable personalities such as Candy Jim Taylor, Canute R. Matson, and Cap Anson, who all passed away in Chicago.
Colombo, the largest city of Sri Lanka, serves as a significant urban center with distinctive geographical and demographic characteristics. The city covers a total area of 37.31 square kilometers with a land area of 699,000,000 square meters, while its metropolitan area extends across 3,684,000,000 square meters. With a total population of 752,993 residents, Colombo maintains a population density of 20,182 people per square kilometer. The metropolitan area houses a substantially larger population of 5,648,000 inhabitants. Situated at an elevation of 1.0 meter above sea level, Colombo operates within the Sri Lanka Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +05:30. The city's postal code system follows the format 0xxxx, and its area code is 011. Colombo holds particular historical significance as it has served as the capital for multiple political entities, including British Ceylon, Dutch Ceylon, and the Dominion of Ceylon, reflecting its classification as a location with multiple capitals. The city hosts numerous important institutions and organizations. Educational establishments include the National School of Business Management, while higher education is represented by campuses of the Institute of Bankers of Sri Lanka, the Institute of Higher National Diploma in Engineering, and the Sri Lanka Institute of Advanced Technological Education. Notable schools within the city include Carey College, Colombo and Methodist College, Colombo. The Satyn magazine is also based in Colombo. Military presence in the city includes garrisons of the Colombo Town Guard, Sri Lanka Air Force, and Sri Lanka Army Women's Corps. Several sports clubs maintain their grounds in Colombo, including Java Lane SC, Ratnam SC, and Nandimithra SC. The city serves as headquarters for various political organizations such as the Prime Minister's Office of Sri Lanka, Bodu Bala Sena, and the Democratic National Alliance. Major corporations with operations in Colombo include CameraLK, Cargills Bank, Carson Cumberbatch, Royal Ceramics, and Sampath Bank. Colombo has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Carl van Geyzel, Carlo Fonseka, and Ameena Hussein. The city has also been the final resting place for prominent figures such as Camillus Perera, Carlo Fonseka, and Prasanna Jayawardena. Various personalities have received their education in Colombo, including Umaria Sinhawansa, J. C. A. Corea, and Granville Rodrigo. The city has been home to numerous residents and natives, including Ryan Henderlin, Bathiya and Santhush, Nimal Mendis, Cassim Faizal, Dayasiri Jayasekara, and John Seneviratne. Historical events have also taken place in Colombo, including the Battle of Mulleriyawa and the Easter Sunday Raid. The President's House, Colombo stands as a significant landmark within the city. Additionally, Pillayan's second tenure had a predecessor connection to Colombo.
Conakry serves as the capital city of Guinea and has historically functioned as the capital for French Guinea and throughout Guinea's history. This major urban center covers a total area of 450.0 square kilometers and houses a population of 1,660,973 residents. The city operates on Universal Time Coordinated with a UTC offset of ±0. The city holds significant political and historical importance, having been the site of major events including the 1984 Guinean coup d'état, the 2021 Guinean coup d'état, and Operation Green Sea. Several notable monuments and landmarks are located within Conakry, including the Monument du 22 Novembre 1970. The hospitality sector is represented by establishments such as Hotel Mariador Palace and Hotel Palm Camayenne. Conakry has served as the birthplace for several prominent individuals, including Pépé Guilavogui, Sambégou Bangoura, and Saïdou Sow. The city has also been the final resting place for notable figures such as Joseph Saidu Momoh, Claude Kory Kondiano, and Mohamed Ofei Sylla. Current residents of the city include political figures Cellou Dalein Diallo, Fodéba Isto Keira, and Shekuba Saccoh. The city serves as an important transportation hub, with Ahmed Sékou Touré International Airport located within its boundaries. Union des Transports Africains de Guinée operates with Conakry as its hub airport. The sports landscape includes several football clubs that call the city home, including Horoya AC, Tabounsou FC, and Satellite FC, all of which use Conakry as their ground. Political organizations have established their headquarters in the capital, including the Democratic Party of Guinea – African Democratic Rally and the Unity and Progress Party. The aviation sector is represented by Eagle Air (Guinea), which maintains its headquarters in the city. Military presence is established through the Republican Guard of Guinea, which maintains its garrison in Conakry. Geographically, Conakry's strategic location places it as the nearest city to both Baie de Sangareya and the Atlantic Ocean, highlighting its coastal position and importance as a maritime gateway for the country.
Copenhagen, the capital city of Denmark, is a major metropolitan area with significant demographic and geographic characteristics. The city has a total area of 183.2 square kilometers and supports a population of 1,366,301 residents, resulting in a population density of 4,417.65 people per square kilometer. The urban area extends across 525,500,000 square meters, while the broader metropolitan region encompasses an impressive 3,371,800,000 square meters. The metropolitan population reaches 2,135,634 inhabitants, creating a metropolitan density of 633.38 people per square kilometer. Residents of Copenhagen are known as Copenhageners, and the city operates under the area code (+45) 3. Postal services cover a range of codes including 1050–1778, 2100, 2150, 2200, 2300, 2400, 2450, and 2500. The city observes both Central European Time and Central European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +01:00 and +02:00 respectively. Copenhagen has been the location of several notable structures and establishments, including the Capernaum Church, the Bellavista housing estate, and the Povl Badstuber House. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, particularly three battles that took place in 1289, 1801, and 1807, all bearing the name Battle of Copenhagen. The Danish capital has served as both birthplace and final resting place for numerous notable individuals. Among those born in Copenhagen are Caja Heimann, Camilla Overbye Roos, and Camille Rasmussen. The city has also been the place of death for several prominent figures, including Camillus Nyrop, Canute Porse the Elder, and Carl Aarsleff.
Cotonou, the largest city in Benin, is a significant urban center located in West Africa with a total area of 79.0 square kilometers and an elevation of 51.0 meters above sea level. The city has a substantial population of 2,401,067 residents, making it a major demographic hub in the country. The city serves as an important location for various organizations and institutions. The West African Power Pool maintains both its location and headquarters in Cotonou, while other organizations such as Miss Bénin and the Marxist–Leninist Communist Party of Benin also have their headquarters there. Additionally, Elan Coton operates from the city, and the Stade René Pleven d'Akpakpa is situated within its boundaries. Cotonou has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Rodrigue Akpakoun, Basile Adjou Moumouni, and Patrice Djokoué. The city has also served as the final resting place for prominent figures such as Rosine Vieyra Soglo, Simon Bikindi, and Hubert Maga. The city plays a crucial role in aviation, with Cadjehoun Airport located there. Two airlines, Aero Benin and COTAIR, use Cotonou as their hub airport, highlighting the city's importance as a transportation center. Educational institutions are well-represented in Cotonou, with several notable establishments calling the city home. The University of Science and Technology of Benin and the Établissement Français d'Enseignement Montaigne are both located there, while CIFAD maintains a campus in the city. Sports culture thrives in Cotonou, with multiple football clubs using the city as their ground, including JA Cotonou, Lions de l'Atakory, and Ajijas Cotonou. The city's proximity to the Bight of Benin, which considers Cotonou its nearest city, further emphasizes its strategic coastal location in the region.
Dakar serves as the capital city of Senegal and stands as a significant urban center in West Africa. The city covers a total area of 83.0 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 22.0 meters above sea level. With a total population of 1,146,052 residents, Dakar maintains a population density of 12,510.0 people per square kilometer. The broader metropolitan area encompasses 3,938,358 inhabitants, resulting in a metropolitan population density of 4,484.0 people per square kilometer. The city operates on Greenwich Mean Time with a UTC offset of +0. Dakar's historical importance extends beyond its current role as Senegal's capital, having previously served as the capital of both French West Africa and the Mali Federation. This strategic position has made it a focal point for various institutions and organizations throughout its history. The city hosts numerous educational institutions, including Dakar Bourguiba University and Université du Sahel, while Blaise Diagne International Airport serves the metropolitan area. Several notable organizations maintain their headquarters in Dakar, including Rewmi, the Liberation Front of Portuguese Guinea and Cape Verde, and Transair (Senegal). The telecommunications company Sonatel also has its location in the city, and the French Navy and Red Guard of Senegal maintain garrisons there. Dakar's cultural significance is reflected through events such as the Dakar Biennale and institutions like the Pasteur Institute of Dakar. The city has strong connections to sports, with several football clubs including Dakar Université Club, US Ouakam, and Étoile Lusitana using it as their ground, while the basketball team US Gorée is also located there. The city has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Candice Gilg, Qasem Burhan, and Robert Lopez Mendy. It has also been the final resting place for prominent figures such as Carole Fredericks, Samba Félix Ndiaye, and Biri Biri. Additionally, Dakar has served as an educational destination for individuals like Emmanuel Bombande and Alassane Diago, while being the hometown of cultural figures including Rudgy Pajany, Alioune Mbaye Nder, and Pee Froiss. The city's strategic location is further emphasized by its proximity to the Atlantic Ocean, which considers Dakar its nearest city. Dakar has also been the site of significant historical events, including the Battle of Dakar. The city's industrial connections include serving as an assembly location for the IKCO Samand vehicle, while Louis Diène Faye has professional occupation ties to the city.
Damascus, the capital city of Syria, stands as the country's largest city with a total population of 2,503,000 residents. Located at an elevation of 680 meters above sea level, the city covers a total area of 105 square kilometers, while its urban area extends across an impressive 77 million square meters. The city operates under the area code system with country code 963 and city code 11, and follows UTC+3 time zone. Throughout history, Damascus has served as the capital for several significant political entities, including the Umayyad Caliphate, the Arab Kingdom of Syria, and Aram-Damascus. The city has been the site of numerous military engagements, including the Capture of Damascus in 1920, the Qaboun offensive in 2017, and the Battle of Al-Malihah. The 17th Horse (Poona Horse) also fought battles in Damascus. Damascus serves as the headquarters and location for several Syrian government ministries, including the Ministry of Agriculture and Agrarian Reform, the Ministry of Communications and Technology, and the Ministry of Expatriates. The city has also been home to various military garrisons, including the Defense Companies, the Republican Guard, and the VIII Corps of the Ottoman Empire. The city has been the birthplace of notable individuals such as Caresse Bashar, Ammar Abd Rabbo, and Qadri Jamil, while also serving as the final resting place for Amer Husni Lutfi, Sami Pasha al-Farouqi, and Sami al-Jundi. Several prominent figures have called Damascus their hometown, including Mohamad Bash, MAias Alyamani, and Hewar, while others like Bassam Tohme, Salam Safaf, and Ghassan al-Zamel have established their residence there. Damascus has hosted major sporting events, including the 1976 and 1992 Pan Arab Games, and is home to Barada SC football club. The city's cultural significance extends to its linguistic heritage, as Western Neo-Aramaic is spoken there, and it has connections to various cultural elements including the Nur al-Din Madrasa and The Mirrors of Fire. The city's culinary traditions are represented by regional specialties such as Booza, Barazek, and Zhourat shamia, which originates from Damascus. Additionally, the city houses Damascus Hospital and serves as the assembly location for IKCO Samand vehicles. Mikhail Mishaqa is particularly known for his association with Damascus, and the Syrian opposition also recognizes Damascus as its largest city.
Dangriga is a town located in Belize with a population of 9,593 residents, who are known as Dangrigans. Situated at sea level with an elevation of 0.0, the town operates in the Central Time zone with a UTC offset of -6. The town holds significance as the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Maxime Faget, Theodore Aranda, and Osmond P. Martin. Theodore Aranda maintains his residence in Dangriga, as does Ivan Ramos. The town also served as the final resting place for Thomas Vincent Ramos, who died there. Dangriga features several important landmarks and facilities. The Drums of Our Fathers Monument is located within the town, while Dangriga Airport serves the community's aviation needs. The town is home to Revolutionary Conquerors FC, a football club that uses Dangriga as their ground. The town's coastal location makes it the nearest city to several significant marine areas. Glover's Reef, the Gulf of Honduras, and the South Water Caye Marine Reserve all consider Dangriga their closest urban center, highlighting the town's strategic position along Belize's coastline and its importance as a gateway to the country's marine resources.
Delhi is a state and union territory of India with a total area of 1,484.063187222528 square kilometers and a water area of 17,870,917.9613184 square meters. The territory sits at an elevation of 198.12 meters and has a total population of 16,787,941 people, resulting in a population density of 11,312.02104097658 people per square kilometer. Delhi operates under Indian Standard Time with a UTC offset of +5.30 and is administered by the Government of Delhi as its governing body. The region serves as the location for several significant infrastructure facilities, including the Pragati-III Combined Cycle Power Plant and the Pragati-I Combined Cycle Gas Power Station. Additionally, Punjab National Bank is located in Delhi, establishing the territory as an important financial center. Delhi has been the site of numerous historical military engagements, including the Capture of Delhi in 1771, the Battle of Badli-ki-Serai, and the Battle of Delhi in 1757. These events underscore the territory's strategic importance throughout Indian history. The region has also been significant as both a birthplace and final resting place for notable individuals. Delhi is the birthplace of director Amit Sharma, musician Prabh Deep, and actress Prachi Tehlan. Conversely, it served as the place of death for scholar Camille Bulcke, former President Pranab Mukherjee, and Prateek Chaudhuri, reflecting the territory's role as a center of cultural and political activity in India.
Dhaka, the capital city of Bangladesh, serves as both the nation's capital and largest city. This major urban center operates under a Mayor-Council government system and is administered by two governing bodies: the Dhaka North City Corporation and the Dhaka South City Corporation. The city spans an urban area of 305,470,000 square meters, while its metropolitan area covers an extensive 2,161,168,958.883889 square meters. With a metropolitan population of 21,741,090 residents, Dhaka maintains a population density of 29,373 people per unit area. The inhabitants of this bustling metropolis are known as Dhakaiyas. Situated at an elevation of 31.991808 meters, Dhaka operates in the Bangladesh Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +6. The city's postal system uses codes including 1000, 1100, 12xx, and 13xx to serve its various districts and neighborhoods. Dhaka's significance extends far beyond its current role as Bangladesh's capital, as it also served as the capital of the historical Bengal Subah. The city has been the site of several important historical events, including the Bangladesh Rifles revolt and the 3 November 1975 Bangladeshi coup d'état. The city serves as a major financial and commercial hub, hosting the headquarters of numerous organizations including the Cabinet Committee on Public Purchase, Bengal Group of Industries, and Progressive Democratic Party. Financial institutions such as Bengal Commercial Bank Limited and Pubali Bank have established their operations in Dhaka, while Royal Bengal Airline uses the city as its hub airport. Dhaka's educational landscape is particularly robust, with numerous institutions calling the city home. The Royal University of Dhaka and Gono University are located within the state, while Government Saadat College operates in the area. Several universities have established their main campuses or presence in Dhaka, including Bangladesh Home Economics College, Government College of Applied Human Science, and the Institute of Cost and Management Accountants of Bangladesh. The Canadian University of Bangladesh, Presidency University Bangladesh, and Prime University are all situated in the city. The city has significant connections to notable individuals throughout history. Prafulla Chandra Ghosh, Prafulla Roy, and Prarthana Fardin Dighi were all born in Dhaka, while the city served as the final resting place for Begum Feroza Bari, Qayyum Chowdhury, and Qazi Abdul Alim. Shayan Chowdhury Arnob received his education in Dhaka, and architect Brian MacKay-Lyons has created significant buildings in the city. Dhaka also plays an important role in Bangladesh's defense infrastructure, serving as a garrison for the Counter Terrorism and Intelligence Bureau, Bangladesh Naval Aviation, and the Bangladesh Navy. The city's sporting facilities host various teams and events, including the 2019-20 Bangladesh Police FC season, the 2020-21 Abahani Limited Dhaka season, and matches for the Bangladesh national under-19 cricket team. Additionally, Dhaka serves as a manufacturing center, with the Toyota Corolla E120 being assembled in the city, and the Purbachal Expressway providing important transportation infrastructure for the metropolitan area.
Djibouti City, located in the country of Djibouti, serves as a significant urban center with a total area of 26.0 square kilometers and an expansive urban area covering 44,000,000.0 square meters. The city sits at an elevation of 14.0 meters above sea level and has a total population of 600,000 residents. Operating in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3, the city uses the area code +253 for telecommunications. The city serves as home to several important institutions and facilities. El Hadj Hassan Gouled Aptidon Stadium is located within Djibouti City, as are key government and financial institutions including the Ministry of Defence and Exim Bank. The city also functions as the headquarters for multiple political organizations, including the People's Rally for Progress, Union for National Salvation, and Union for the Presidential Majority. Djibouti City has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Mohamed Ali Fourchette, Mumin Gala, and Mahamoud Ali Youssouf. The city has also served as the final resting place for prominent figures such as Mohamed Ali Fourchette, Ahmed Dini Ahmed, and Abdo Xamar Qoodh. Currently, the city serves as the residence for Mumin Gala and Ayanleh Souleiman, while Abdallah Lee considers it his hometown. The city's strategic location is highlighted by its proximity to the Gulf of Tadjoura, for which Djibouti City serves as the nearest major urban center. This positioning contributes to the city's role as an important hub in the region.
Dodoma serves as the capital city of Tanzania, positioned at an elevation of 1,120 meters above sea level. The city encompasses a substantial land area of 2,576,000,000 square meters and supports a total population of 2,245,800 residents. Dodoma operates within the East Africa Time zone, maintaining a UTC offset of +3, and uses the area code 026 for telecommunications. As Tanzania's capital, Dodoma hosts several important government institutions. The Ministry of Energy, Ministry of Foreign Affairs and East African Cooperation, and Ministry of Health and Social Welfare all maintain their headquarters and primary locations within the city. This concentration of governmental offices reflects Dodoma's central role in Tanzania's administrative structure. The city has educational significance as well, housing multiple higher education institutions including the University of Dodoma and St. John's University of Tanzania. Transportation infrastructure is provided by Msalato International Airport, which serves the city and surrounding region. Dodoma has connections to various notable individuals throughout Tanzanian history. The city served as the birthplace for Rogers Mtagwa, Renaida Braun, and Mohamed Husseini. Conversely, it was the place of death for Horace Kolimba, John William Kijazi, and Richard Ndassa. Currently, Davis G. Mwamfupe and Alphaxard Lugola maintain their residence in Dodoma. The city also supports sporting activities, serving as the home ground for two football clubs: JKT Ruvu Stars and Polisi Dodoma. These various aspects—governmental, educational, transportation, residential, and recreational—combine to establish Dodoma as a significant urban center within Tanzania.
Doha, the capital city of Qatar, spans a total area of 132.0 square kilometers and has a population of 2,382,000 residents. The city operates on UTC+3 time zone, serving as the political and administrative center of the nation. The city houses numerous important government and cultural institutions. The Amiri Diwan of the State of Qatar, Qatar Amateur Radio Society, and Qatar Basketball Federation are all located within Doha's boundaries. Several educational institutions have established their presence there, including Carnegie Mellon University in Qatar, Qatar National Theater, and Qatar University. The city also serves as headquarters for major corporations such as Qatar Airways, Qatar Chamber of Commerce and Industry, and Qatar Executive. Doha has been the site of significant political events throughout Qatar's history, including the 1972 and 1995 Qatari coups d'état, as well as the 1996 coup attempt. The city continues to play a central role in the country's governance and development. Several notable individuals have connections to Doha through birth, death, or residence. Saud Al Hajiri, Homam Ahmed, and Hussein Yasser were all born in the city, while Christian Benítez, Frederiek Nolf, and Yusuf al-Qaradawi passed away there. Current residents include Chris Eaton, Vyacheslav Skoromnov, and Abdul Rahman bin Hamad Al Attiyah. The city's sports scene is vibrant, with El Jaish SC and Al-Arabi FC Qatar Reserves using Doha as their home ground, and the 2011-12 Al Sadd SC season also being played there. The Oryx Cup tournament takes place in the country with Doha as its base. Additionally, the Qatari Emiri Navy maintains a garrison in the city. Doha's growing prominence extends to various business sectors, with companies like Es'hailSat, Mosafer, and Meddy establishing their operations there. The city serves as a regional hub for international businesses, including Morgans Hotel Group and Fakhro Group. The cultural landscape has also been enriched by architectural contributions from John McAslan, who has significant buildings in the city, and Michel Mossessian, who has undertaken significant projects there. Even the music industry has found its way to Doha, with Jungkook's song "Dreamers" being recorded in the city.
Douala is Cameroon's largest city, covering a total area of 210.0 square kilometers at an elevation of 13.0 meters above sea level. The city has a substantial population of 5,768,400 residents and operates in the West Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +1. The city serves as a significant location for various landmarks and institutions. Notable structures include the Bonakouamouang Chimney, Brasseries du Cameroun, and Villa Mandessi Bell, all situated within Douala. The city is also home to educational facilities such as CAE Oxford Aviation Academy Douala, which has both its campus and city designation in Douala. Transportation infrastructure includes Douala International Airport, which serves the city. Douala has produced several notable individuals, with Carlos Baleba, Carlos Kameni, and Carlos Takam all being born there. The city has also been the final resting place for Samuel Wembé, Bertrand Teyou, and Defao, who all died in Douala. Additionally, entertainers Mister Bibal and Stanley Enow consider Douala their hometown. The city supports various sports teams, with Léopard Douala, Union Douala, and Douala Athletic Club all using Douala as their home ground. Several major companies have established their headquarters in the city, including Camair-Co, Cameroon Airlines, and Camrail. Linguistically, the Duala language is spoken in Douala, reflecting the city's cultural heritage. The nearby Douala Edéa National Park lists Douala as its nearest city, highlighting the area's natural attractions. Interestingly, the city of Bandjoun shares the same time zone designation as Douala, indicating regional time coordination.
Dubai is a metropolis located in the United Arab Emirates with a total area of 1,610.0 square kilometers and a population of 3,515,813 residents. The city operates in the Time in the United Arab Emirates time zone with a UTC offset of +04:00. People from Dubai are known as Dubaians, and the city was founded by Al Maktoum. Dubai functions under an absolute monarchy form of government. The city serves as the location for several notable entities and events. Camp Mirage is situated in Dubai, as is the television programme Capital Connection. The Pragma Group also has its location there, and the Hyacinth incident took place in the city. Dubai has been the birthplace of several individuals, including Carla Rahal, Amina Taher, and Qasim Zubair. The city has also been the place where notable deaths occurred, serving as the death place for Bill Duff, an Arabist, as well as being associated with the Death of Lee Bradley Brown and the death of Derek Khan.
Dublin, the capital city of the Republic of Ireland, is a significant urban center with a total area of 117.8 square kilometers and an urban area spanning 318,000,000 square meters. The city has a total population of 554,554 residents, resulting in a population density of 4,708 people per square kilometer, while the broader metropolitan area is home to 1,417,700 inhabitants. The city operates under the area code 01 (+3531) and uses postal codes ranging from D01 to D18, D20, D22, D24, and D6W. Dublin observes both Greenwich Mean Time (GMT) and Irish Standard Time, with UTC offsets of 0 and +1 respectively, depending on the season. Dublin's official motto, "The Obedience of the citizens produces a happy city," is alternatively translated as "An Obedient Citizenry Produces a Happy City," reflecting the city's civic values and heritage. The city serves as a significant business location, housing companies such as Cadbury Ireland and Cairn Homes. Dublin is also notable for its geographic features, including Camden Street, which is located within the city. Throughout its history, Dublin has been the site of several important military engagements, including the Battle of Dublin, the Battle of Mount Street Bridge, and the Siege of Dublin in 1649. The city has been both a birthplace and final resting place for many notable individuals. Among those born in Dublin are Cahir Davitt, Caitriona Beggs, and Caitríona Balfe, while the city also served as the place of death for Caitlín Brugha, Campbell Armstrong, and Carew Arthur Meredith.
Dushanbe, the capital city of Tajikistan, is a significant urban center with a total population of 863,400 people. The city covers a land area of 203,182,500 square meters, with its urban area spanning 185,000,000 square meters. Situated at an elevation of 823 meters above sea level, Dushanbe operates in the Tajikistan Time zone with a UTC offset of +5 and uses the area code 372. Throughout its history, Dushanbe has served as the capital for multiple political entities, including the Tajik Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic and the Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic, before becoming the capital of modern Tajikistan. The city hosts numerous important institutions and organizations, with the Committee of Emergency Situations and Civil Defense of Tajikistan, the Rudaki Institute of Language and Literature, the Party of People's Unity, and the People's Democratic Party of Tajikistan all maintaining their headquarters there. The city's hospitality sector includes notable establishments such as Hotel Tajikistan and the Hyatt Regency Dushanbe Hotel. Educational institutions in Dushanbe encompass QSI International School of Dushanbe and the Mastibek Tashmukhamedov Military Lyceum of the Ministry of Defense of Tajikistan, while Ivan Mikoyan received his education in the city. Dushanbe serves as an important military center, with several units garrisoned there, including the 134th Motor Rifle Division, the Russian 201st Military Base, and the 7th Airborne Assault Brigade. The city's sports infrastructure includes grounds for various football clubs such as Varzob Dushanbe, DISI Invest Dushanbe, and Dynamo Dushanbe, and it serves as the stadium location for the Tajikistan national under-20 football team. The financial sector is represented by institutions like Spitamen Bank and Kont Bank, both located in the city. Dushanbe is also connected to regional transportation networks through the Peshawar–Kabul–Dushanbe motorway. Several notable individuals have connections to Dushanbe as their place of birth, including Denis Knitel, Pavel Harçik, and Umarali Quvvatov. The city is also the hometown of prominent figures such as Shoista Mullojonova, Daler Nazarov, and Karomatullo Qurbonov. Additionally, various individuals maintain residence in Dushanbe, including Abdul Latif Pedram, Svetlana Gerasimenko, and Shahriyor Daminov. The city has also been the final resting place for several significant figures, including Qahhor Mahkamov, Victor Nilsen, and Mirzo Tursunzoda.
Faisalabad is a city district of Pakistan founded by James Broadwood Lyall. Located in Pakistan, the city has a total area of 1326.073912492032 square kilometers, with land covering 841746135.8592 square meters and water areas spanning 427348038.20544 square meters, representing 33.0 percent of the total area. The metropolitan area extends across 5855963117.469696 square meters. Situated at an elevation of 186.0 meters, Faisalabad has a total population of 3204726 residents, who are known as Faisalabadis. The city operates under the Pakistan Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +05:00. Its postal code system uses the format 38xxx, while the area code is 041. Faisalabad serves as a significant educational hub, hosting several institutions including the University of Agriculture, Faisalabad, University of Engineering and Technology Faisalabad Campus, University of Faisalabad, and University Medical and Dental College Faisalabad, all of which have their campuses or are located in the city. The Pakistan Institute of Public Finance Accountants also maintains a campus there. The city houses various educational and administrative organizations, with Sandal College Faisalabad and the Board of Intermediate and Secondary Education, Faisalabad located within its boundaries. The Board of Intermediate and Secondary Education, Faisalabad has its headquarters in the city and serves the Faisalabad region. Other organizations headquartered in Faisalabad include City 41 and the District Bar Association Faisalabad, which also serves the local region. Faisalabad has connections to several notable individuals. Romesh Chandra, Samar Ishaq, and poet Mohan Singh were all born in the city, while Sardar Ahmad Chishti, Bari Nizami, and Muhammad Fazal Karim died there. Bari Nizami considered Faisalabad his hometown, and Raja Nadir Pervez maintains his residence in the city. The city serves as an important industrial center, particularly in automotive manufacturing, with several Hyundai vehicle models assembled there, including the sixth generation Hyundai Elantra AD, Hyundai Porter, and third generation Hyundai Tucson TL. Additionally, Faisalabad houses the Borstal Institution and Juvenile Jail Faisalabad, Allied Hospital, and serves as the location city for Faisalabad Electric Supply Company.
Freetown, the capital city and municipality of Sierra Leone, stands as a significant urban center with a rich history and diverse institutional presence. Founded on March 11, 1792, the city sits at an elevation of 26.0 meters and covers a total area of 81.48 square kilometers. Operating under Greenwich Mean Time and governed by a city council system, Freetown supports a substantial population of 1,055,964 residents, with its metropolitan area encompassing 1,500,234 people. The city has served as the capital for multiple iterations of Sierra Leone's political structure, including Sierra Leone from 1961 to 1971 and the former Sierra Leone Colony and Protectorate. This historical significance is reflected in its role as headquarters for several important organizations, including the Unity Party of Sierra Leone, the Ministry of Defence and National Security, and the Face of Sierra Leone IAMSL Organization. Freetown's financial sector is represented by major institutions such as Union Trust Bank and Rokel Commercial Bank, both located within the city. The educational landscape includes prominent institutions like Limkokwing University of Creative Technology, which maintains a campus there, along with the Institute of Public Administration and Management and Milton Margai College of Education and Technology. The city's transportation infrastructure connects it to broader regional networks through Lungi International Airport, while aviation companies Eagle Air of Guinea and Weasua Air Transport utilize Freetown as a target airport and hub airport respectively. Military presence is maintained through garrisons of the Commander-in-Chief South Atlantic and Flag Officer West Africa. Freetown's cultural and sporting life is vibrant, with football clubs Golf Leopards F.C., Ports Authority F.C., and Central Parade F.C. all using the city as their home ground. The music scene includes notable artists such as Daddy Saj, Freddy Will, and Bajah + The Dry Eye Crew, who call Freetown their hometown. The city has been home to numerous notable individuals throughout its history. Prince Barrie, surgeon Robert Smith, and Roda Antar were all born in Freetown, while Robert Smith also died there, along with Bertha Conton and Patrick Daniel Koroma. Current residents include Sam Franklyn Gibson, Sam Sesay, and Samuel Sam-Sumana, while Gibril Sesay maintains his occupation there. Freetown's historical importance extends to significant events like the Siege of Freetown, and it is associated with abolitionist John Clarkson's notable work. The city's natural setting places it near both the Western Area Peninsula National Park and the Atlantic Ocean, while the Sacred Heart Cathedral stands as an important religious landmark within the city itself.
Funafuti is an atoll located in Tuvalu with a total area of 2.4 square kilometers and a population of 6,320 residents. This significant landmass serves as both the capital and largest city of Tuvalu, and it previously functioned as the capital of the Gilbert and Ellice Islands. The atoll hosts several important institutions and facilities that serve the nation. Princess Margaret Hospital provides medical services to the community, while the Tuvalu Sports Ground offers recreational facilities. The Tuvalu Telecommunications Corporation operates from Funafuti, alongside other key organizations including the Tuvalu National Library and Archives and the Tuvalu Meteorological Service, all of which maintain their headquarters on the atoll. Educational opportunities are available through Fetuvalu Secondary School, and visitors can find accommodation at the Vaiaku Lagi Hotel. The sporting community is well-represented with three football clubs—Nui F.C., Lakena United, and F.C. Manu Laeva—all using Funafuti as their home ground. Funafuti has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Etimoni Timuani, Fiatau Penitala Teo, and Ionatana Ionatana. The atoll has also been the final resting place for prominent figures such as Elisala Pita, Apisai Ielemia, and Toaripi Lauti. Additionally, Toakai Puapua maintains residence there. The atoll's historical significance extends to military events, as George F. Good Jr. participated in a battle at Funafuti, highlighting the location's role in broader Pacific conflicts.
Geneva, a Swiss city with an elevation of 375.0 meters, serves as the location for several notable organizations and events. The city is governed by mayor Frédérique Perler and encompasses a total area of 15.86 square kilometers. Geneva's postal code system includes 1200, or 1201–09 Genève, 1213 Petit-Lancy, and 1227 Les Acacias. The city shares borders with several neighboring municipalities, including Carouge, Pregny-Chambésy, and Vernier, Switzerland. Residents of Geneva are known by the demonyms Genevan or Genevese, as well as Genevois(e). Geneva has established itself as an important location for various organizations and sporting events. The Programme for the Endorsement of Forest Certification is based there, along with the Rolex Trophy and Rugby Club CERN. The city has also been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Caecilia Charbonnier, Carlos Franz, and Spanish footballer Carlos Varela. Additionally, Geneva served as the final resting place for prominent figures such as anatomist Carl Bergmann, Carl Vogt, and Carlo Ponti, all of whom died in the city.
Georgetown, Guyana serves as the capital city of Guyana and was founded on April 29, 1812. Located at sea level with an elevation of 0.0 meters, the city covers a total area of 70.0 square kilometers and has a population of 118,363 residents. Georgetown operates in the UTC-4 time zone. The city holds significant historical importance, having served as the capital not only of modern Guyana but also of the former British Guiana and Demerara. This rich colonial heritage is reflected throughout the urban landscape and institutional framework. Georgetown is home to several notable landmarks and structures, including the Umana Yana, Company Path Garden, and Georgetown Cenotaph, all of which contribute to the city's cultural and historical character. The city also houses important healthcare facilities such as Georgetown Public Hospital and St. Joseph Mercy Hospital. The educational landscape of Georgetown is robust, featuring prominent institutions including Queen's College, Bishops' High School, and the University of Guyana. These establishments serve the broader educational needs of the region and contribute to the city's role as an academic center. Georgetown has produced several notable individuals across various fields. The city served as the birthplace of boxer Carl Crawford, as well as Carl Gouveia and Carl Hooper. Conversely, it was the place where Carl Bovallius, Sase Narain, and Berkeley Gaskin passed away. Additionally, Saint Jhn and Norman Madhoo consider Georgetown their hometown. The city serves as an important economic and administrative hub, hosting the headquarters of several significant organizations including the People's National Congress Reform, Civic, and the Ministry of Education. Major companies such as Guyana Power and Light and the National Milling Company of Guyana maintain their operations in Georgetown. Georgetown's sporting culture is represented by several football clubs that use the city as their home ground, including Pele FC, Western Tigers FC, and Georgetown FC, demonstrating the city's active participation in regional athletics and community sports.
Guatemala City serves as the capital city of Guatemala and stands as the country's largest urban center. This municipality operates under a municipal government type and is located within the Guatemala Department. The city encompasses a total area of 220.0 square kilometers with no water area, situated at an elevation of 1,500 meters above sea level. Guatemala City operates in the Central America time zone with a UTC offset of −06:00. The metropolitan area houses a population of 3,052,521 residents, while the city proper contains 994,938 inhabitants, resulting in a population density of 4,522 people per square kilometer. The city's official mottos reflect its civic identity: "Todos somos la ciudad" (We are all the city) and "Tú eres la ciudad" (You are the city). Guatemala City's historical significance extends beyond its current role, having previously served as the capital of both the Federal Republic of Central America and the Captaincy General of Guatemala. The city hosts several notable cultural and architectural landmarks, including the Carrera Theater, San José Castle, and a relief map of Guatemala, all located within its boundaries. The city serves as an important educational hub, housing multiple universities including Rafael Landívar University, Universidad Mesoamericana, Universidad Mariano Gálvez, and Universidad de San Carlos de Guatemala, all of which maintain campuses or facilities within the city. Sports facilities are also present, with Universidad SC and Aurora F.C. both maintaining their grounds in Guatemala City. Several prominent media organizations have established their headquarters in the capital, including Canal 13 television channel, Prensa Libre newspaper, and the Progressive Liberal Party. The Presidential Honor Guard maintains its garrison within the city limits. Guatemala City has been the birthplace of notable individuals including Carlos Alberto Mijangos, footballer Carlos Castillo, and Carlos Figueroa. The city has also been home to various residents throughout history, including former presidents Carlos Manuel Arana Osorio, politicians Roxana Baldetti and Josué Enríquez. Tragically, it has also been the place of death for several significant figures, including Carlos Castillo Armas, Carlos Manuel Arana Osorio, and Próspero Penados del Barrio. The city's cultural scene includes musicians who call it home, such as Carlos Peña, the band Bohemia Suburbana, and singer Gaby Moreno. Additionally, Rafael Yela Günther created notable work related to Guatemala City. The city's political importance continues today, having hosted mayoral elections in both 2019 and 2023.
Guayaquil is a major city in Ecuador that was founded by Francisco de Orellana on July 25, 1535. The city operates under a mayor form of government and has adopted the motto "Por Guayaquil Independiente" (For Independent Guayaquil). Residents of the city are known as Guayaquileños. Geographically, Guayaquil sits at an elevation of 4.0 meters and covers a total area of 344.4943185557914 square kilometers. The city's land area spans 316,418,847.4397491 square meters, while its water area encompasses 28,075,471.11604224 square meters. The metropolitan area extends much further, covering 2,493,860,000.0 square meters. The city uses the postal code EC090150 and the area code (0)4. The population of Guayaquil proper totals 2,698,077 residents, while the metropolitan area is home to 3,113,725 people. The city operates in the Ecuador Time zone with a UTC offset of −5. Guayaquil has served as the location for numerous tennis tournaments, including the 2009, 2010, and 2011 Challenger Ciudad de Guayaquil events. The city has also been the site of several significant military engagements, including the Battle of Cruces, the Battle of Guayaquil, and the Battle of Punta Malpelo. Historically, it served as the capital of the Free Province of Guayaquil. The city has been the birthplace of several notable figures, including Camila Romero, Carlos Alberto Arroyo del Río, and Carlos Arboleda. It has also been the final resting place for prominent individuals such as Carlos González-Artigas, Carlos Julio Arosemena Monroy, and Carlos Julio Arosemena Tola. Additionally, Félix Arauz received an award from Guayaquil, and Marcel Jacobo Laniado de Wind has a child connection to the city. Guayaquil serves as an important educational and transportation hub, housing the Universidad de Especialidades Espíritu Santo and being served by José Joaquín de Olmedo International Airport. The city hosted the 1993 Copa América Final and provided educational opportunities for figures like Álvaro Noboa. Several sports teams call Guayaquil home, including Deportivo Español (Ecuador), L.D. Estudiantil, and C.D. Everest, all of which use the city as their ground. Various organizations have established their headquarters there, including Hogar de Cristo, Guayaquil, DHL Ecuador, and the Concentration of People's Forces. The city has produced and attracted numerous artists and musicians, serving as the hometown for the band Prime Ministers, singer Julio Jaramillo, and performer Mirella Cesa. Athletes Roberto Quiroz, Andrés Gómez, and Kiara Rodriguez maintain residences in Guayaquil. Guayaquil's strategic location makes it significant for maritime activities, as evidenced by the construction of the ship Estramina in 1803. The city's proximity to natural attractions is highlighted by its status as the nearest city to both the Churute Mangroves Ecological Reserve and the Pacific Ocean. Within the city's administrative boundaries lies Mapasingue, which is classified as part of Guayaquil's urban structure.
Gujranwala is a city located in Pakistan that operates under the government type of City Districts of Pakistan. The city covers a total area of 240.0 square kilometers, while its metropolitan area spans an impressive 3,198,000,000.0 square meters. Situated at an elevation of 231.0 meters above sea level, Gujranwala has a total population of 2,027,001 residents. The city serves as an important educational and administrative center, housing several notable institutions. Educational facilities include Quaid-e-Azam Divisional Public School and College and the University of the Punjab, Gujranwala. The city has been the site of notable military engagements, including the Battle of Ramnagar and the Battle of Gujranwala in 1761. Its strategic location is further emphasized by major transportation routes, as both the Grand Trunk Road and the Karachi–Lahore Motorway pass through the city. Harare, the capital city of Zimbabwe and also designated as Harare Province, serves as the country's largest city with a total population of 2,123,132 and a metropolitan population of 3,120,917. The city was officially founded on April 18, 1982, and covers a total area of 940.0 square kilometers at an elevation of 1,490.0 meters above sea level. Residents of the city are known as Harareans, and the area code for the city is 242. Harare operates under a mayor-council government system and follows Central Africa Time with a UTC offset of +2. The city has served as a significant political center throughout the region's history, having been the capital of Rhodesia, Rhodesia (1964–1965), and Company rule in Rhodesia. It was also the largest city of the Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland. The city's political importance continues today, as evidenced by its role as the location of the Parliament of Rhodesia and as the place where the 2017 Zimbabwean coup d'état occurred. Harare hosts numerous important institutions and landmarks, including the National Gallery of Zimbabwe and Morgan Tsvangirai House. The city is home to several educational institutions such as Prince Edward School, St. George's College, and Mazowe Boys High School. The Presidential Guard, Rhodesian Armoured Corps, and Rhodesian Light Infantry maintain garrisons in the city, while various political organizations including the Republican Front and Responsible Government Association, as well as the Rhodesia Prison Service, have established their headquarters there. The city serves as a major transportation hub, with Air Rhodesia and Zimbabwe Express Airlines using it as their hub airport, while Air Trans Africa designates it as a target airport. Harare has also been a center for automotive assembly, with both the Ford F-Series fourth generation and Ford Zephyr being assembled in the city. Several notable individuals have connections to Harare, including those born there such as Calum Price, Campbell Macmillan, and Cara Black, while others like Protais Mpiranya, Rodney Gordon, and Ronald Willson died in the city. The city serves as the residence for prominent figures including David Parirenyatwa, Humphrey Gibbs, and Paul Tangi Mhova Mkondo, and is the hometown of musicians Roki, Mizchif, and Mudiwa Hood. Harare's business landscape includes companies such as Nash Paints and Telecel Zimbabwe, while the medical company Oncocare operates in the region. The city's media presence is represented by radio stations Capitalk 100.4 FM and Power FM Zimbabwe. Sports teams including Black Rhinos F.C., Mashonaland Eagles, and Monomotapa United F.C. use Harare as their ground, contributing to the city's vibrant sporting culture.

Situated at an elevation of 59.0 meters above sea level, Havana's residents are known as Habaneros or Habaneras. Helsinki, the capital city of Finland, was founded on June 12, 1550. The city operates in the Eastern European Time and Eastern European Summer Time zones, with UTC offsets of +02:00 and +03:00 respectively. Helsinki's area code is +358-9, and the urban area spans 680,120,000 square meters. The metropolitan area has a population density of 1.0 per square meter. The city holds significant political and administrative importance, housing key government institutions including the Presidential Palace and the Prime Minister's Office of Finland. Throughout its history, Helsinki has been the site of several notable events and conflicts. The city has been the site of significant military events, including the Battle of Saigon in both 1955 and 1968, as well as the December 1964 South Vietnamese coup. The television series Dead Wrong was filmed on location in Ho Chi Minh City, further highlighting its cultural significance.

Jaipur is a metropolis located in India, founded by Jai Singh II. The city covers a total area of 467.0 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 431.0 meters above sea level. With a population of 4,546,189 residents, the inhabitants are known as Jaipuri or Jaipuriya. The city operates under the Indian Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +05:30, and its postal code system uses the format 3020xx, while the area code is +91-141. The city functions as a municipal corporation, with the Jaipur Municipal Corporation serving as its governing body. This municipal corporation is itself part of the larger Jaipur administrative structure. Historically, Jaipur served as the capital of the former Jaipur State. Jaipur has been shaped by notable architectural contributions, particularly from Vidyadhar Bhattacharya, who worked on significant buildings and projects within the city. The city also has personal connections, as evidenced by Hanut Singh's spousal relationship with Jaipur.
Jakarta, the capital of Indonesia, was founded on June 22, 1527, and serves as one of the country's capital districts and territories. The city operates under Indonesia's subdivision system of government and follows the Time in Indonesia zone with a UTC offset of +07:00. Located at an elevation of 7.9248 meters, Jakarta covers a total area of 664.01 square kilometers and supports a population of 10,609,681 residents, resulting in a population density of 15,978.2 people per square kilometer. This metropolitan region houses 33,430,285 people, creating a metropolitan population density of 4,733 people per square kilometer. Jakarta has served as the location for several notable establishments and businesses, including Cafe Batavia, Cahaya Hati, and California Fried Chicken. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, including the Makassar Uprising, the 30 September Movement, and the APRA coup d'état. The capital has been both a birthplace and final resting place for numerous notable individuals. Among those born in Jakarta are Caisar Putra Aditya, Camelia Malik, and Carla Bio. The city has also been the place of death for several prominent figures, including Caliadi, Carel Reyniersz, and the renowned author Pramoedya Ananta Toer.
Jerusalem is located in Israel and operates under a mayor-council government system, with the Jerusalem Municipality serving as its governing body. The city has a metropolitan population of 1,253,900 residents and sits at an elevation of 754.0 meters above sea level. The city's postal system uses codes beginning with 9XXXXXX, while telephone communications utilize the +972-2 area code. Jerusalem observes multiple time zones throughout the year, including Israel Standard Time and Israel Summer Time, as well as Palestine Summer Time. Correspondingly, the city operates on UTC offsets of both +02:00 and +03:00 depending on the season. Jerusalem holds a unique administrative status as a Corpus separatum, reflecting its special international legal designation. The city serves as the location for several notable organizations, including the Canons Regular of the Holy Sepulchre, Bayit Lepletot, and the Puah Institute. Throughout history, Jerusalem has been the site of significant military events, including the Capture of Jericho, the Sasanian conquest of Jerusalem, and the Battle for Jerusalem. The city has also been the birthplace of several prominent individuals, including Amihai Grosz, Amitai Ziv, and Ron Ben-Yishai. Additionally, Jerusalem served as the final resting place for notable figures such as Benedict I of Jerusalem, Robert Slater, and Robert Weltsch.
Johannesburg is a city located in South Africa that serves as a metropolitan municipality. The city operates under South African Standard Time with a UTC offset of +2 and uses the postal code 2000. Johannesburg can be reached through area codes 010 and 011, and the city's motto is "Unity in development." Geographically, Johannesburg sits at an elevation of 1753.0 meters and covers a total area of 1644.98 square kilometers. The urban area extends significantly larger at 3,357,000,000.0 square meters. The city supports a substantial population, with 5,635,127 residents within the city proper and a metropolitan area population of 10,500,000 people. Several notable structures and establishments are located in Johannesburg, including the Carlton Centre, Carlton Hotel, and Cashtime. Additionally, Campbell Munro, Pro (a South African rapper), and Rodwell Munyenyembe all passed away in Johannesburg.
Kabul, the capital and largest city of Afghanistan, is a municipality with a total area of 1028.24 square kilometers. The city encompasses 1,028,240,000 square meters of land area with no water area, and sits at an elevation of 1,791 meters above sea level. With a total population of 4,601,789 residents, Kabul operates under the UTC+4:30 time zone and uses the area code (+93) 20. The city's postal codes include 100X, 101X, 105X, and 106X. Throughout Afghanistan's complex political history, Kabul has consistently served as the capital for various governmental forms, including the Democratic Republic of Afghanistan, the Republic of Afghanistan (1973–1978), the Emirate of Afghanistan, and the Islamic Republic of Afghanistan. It was also the largest city of the Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan from 1996 to 2001. The city has been the site of numerous significant historical events, including the 1973 Afghan coup d'état, the Siege of Kabul in 1504, and the prolonged Battle of Kabul from 1992 to 1996. Several military installations are located in Kabul, including Camp Eggers, Camp Qargha, and Camp Souter. The city serves as a garrison for various military organizations such as Defense of the Revolution, the Resolute Support Mission, and the Combined Security Transition Command – Afghanistan. Kabul is home to several educational institutions, including Dawat University and Maryam University. The city also hosts the headquarters of multiple political organizations, including the People's Democratic Party of Afghanistan, the People's Islamic Unity Party of Afghanistan, and the United Nations Assistance Mission in Afghanistan. Major businesses with operations in the city include Afghan Wireless and Azizi Bank. The city has produced and attracted numerous notable individuals. Qader Eshpari, Qais Akbar Omar, and Qasim Akhgar were all born in Kabul, though Qasim Akhgar also died there. Other deaths in the city include those of Carsten Thomassen, a journalist, and Qahar Asi. Faiz Muhammad Kateb holds citizenship from Kabul, while several prominent figures maintain residence there, including Olympic athlete Rohullah Nikpai, Roia Zamani, and Sayed Mohammad Ali Jawid. Musicians Mohammad Hussain Sarahang, the band Burka Band, and White City all call Kabul their hometown. The city's sports scene includes several football clubs that use Kabul as their ground, including Sarmi Yashy Kabul F.C., Nijat Kabul F.C., and Ordu Kabul F.C. Transportation infrastructure includes the Peshawar–Kabul–Dushanbe motorway, which passes through the city, and Veteran Avia uses Kabul as a target airport destination. Kabul's cultural diversity is reflected in its linguistic landscape, with the Parachi language being spoken in the city. The nearby Hashmat Khan Park is situated close to Kabul, while various individuals have connections to the city through different relationships, including Ali Ahmad Khan's parental connection and Fakhri Pasha's occupational ties. Jon D. Glassman is particularly known for his association with Kabul.
Kampala serves as the capital city of Uganda and stands as a significant urban center in Sub-Saharan Africa. The city covers a total area of 189 square kilometers, with land comprising 176 million square meters and water areas accounting for 13 million square meters. Situated at an elevation of 1,200 meters, Kampala operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3. The city supports a substantial population, with 1,680,600 residents within its boundaries, resulting in a population density of 8,892 people per square kilometer. The broader metropolitan area encompasses 8.45 billion square meters and houses 6,709,900 people, creating a metropolitan population density of 793 people per square kilometer. Kampala has played a central role throughout Uganda's modern history, serving as the capital during the periods from 1963-1971 and 1979-1986, and continuing as Uganda's capital today. The city has witnessed significant historical events, including the Battle of Kampala, the Fall of Kampala, and the Arube uprising. The city hosts numerous important institutions and organizations. The Capital Markets Authority of Uganda, Rolling Stone Uganda, and the Ministry of Defence and Veterans Affairs Uganda all maintain their headquarters there. Educational institutions with campuses in Kampala include Uganda Christian University, Aga Khan University, Uganda Christian University School of Medicine, and Uganda Management Institute. Medical facilities such as Case Medical Centre, Uganda Heart Institute, and Mulago National Specialised Hospital operate within the region. Several military units have maintained garrisons in Kampala, including the Uganda Army during 1962-1971 and 1971-1980 periods, as well as the Uganda Volunteer Reserve. The city serves as home ground for football clubs Lweza FC, Express FC, and Proline FC, and hosted the 2012 CECAFA Cup Final. Kampala's significance extends to the aviation sector, with MAF Uganda, BAR Aviation Uganda, and Aerolink Uganda all designating it as a target airport. The city's proximity to Lake Victoria further enhances its strategic importance. Notable individuals connected to Kampala include Quiin Abenakyo, Robert Ssejjemba, and Robert Ssentongo, who were all born there. The city has also been the final residence for Roy Mugerwa, Sam Odaka, and Sarah Nyendwoha Ntiro. Current residents include Sam Bitangaro, Sam Byibesho, and Bart Magunda Katureebe. Several prominent figures received their education in Kampala, including Beti Kamya-Turwomwe, Peter Nazareth, and Lilly Adong. The city's vibrant cultural scene includes musical artists such as Sauti Ya Africa, Bebe Cool, and Undercover Brothers Ug, who call Kampala their hometown. Various businesses and organizations have established their presence there, including Appfrica, Fun Factory Uganda, Diamond Trust Bank Uganda, Power of Legacy, and Roke Telkom Uganda. The Buzz Teeniez Awards also take place in the country, with Kampala as its base.

Kathmandu, the capital city of Nepal, serves as the nation's political and cultural center. Founded by Manjushri, the city operates under a mayor-council government system and bears the motto "सांस्कृतिक सहर, काठमाडौं महानगर" (Cultural City, Kathmandu Metropolitan). Kathmandu's strategic location places it near important natural areas, serving as the nearest city to both Shivapuri Nagarjun National Park and Langtang National Park. The city encompasses various neighborhoods and areas, including Samakhushi and Gairidhara, while locations like Pyan Gaun fall within its boundaries. The regional dish Bhutan is associated with the Kathmandu area, reflecting the city's culinary heritage.

The city also functions as the largest city of the East African Community and East African Federation. Geographically, Kinshasa covers a total area of 9,965 square kilometers, with an urban area spanning 600,000,000 square meters. The city sits at an elevation of 240 meters and operates in the West Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +1. Its area code is 243 + 9. The city maintains a population density of 1,462 people per square kilometer, with a total population of 17,071,000 and a metropolitan population of 17,239,463. The Provincial Assembly of Kinshasa serves as the city's governing body and is located within Kinshasa itself. The Republican Guard, Civil Guard (Zaire), and Land Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo all maintain garrisons in Kinshasa. Aviation companies Ligne Aérienne du Roi Albert and Great Lakes Business Company use Kinshasa as their hub airport. Sports culture thrives in Kinshasa, with several football clubs calling the city home. Racing Club Kinshasa, Daring Club Motema Pembe, and FC Renaissance du Congo all have their grounds in Kinshasa, while the DR Congo women's national under-20 football team uses the city as their stadium location. Political and international organizations have established significant presences in Kinshasa. MONUSCO, the Democratic Social Christian Party, and the Unified Lumumbist Party all maintain their headquarters in the city. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, including the December 2013 Kinshasa attacks and Operation Kitona. Healthcare infrastructure in the region includes several major medical facilities. L'hôpital du Cinquantenaire de Kinshasa and Kinshasa General Hospital are both located in the Kinshasa region. The city's geographical significance extends to nearby natural features, with Pool Malebo having Kinshasa as its nearest city and Mount Mangengenge located in the Kinshasa region. Additionally, Sub-Saharan Africa includes Kinshasa among its constituent countries.

La Paz, located in Bolivia, serves as the capital of the country and holds significant historical importance, having also functioned as the capital of both the Republic of Alto Perú and Upper Peru. Founded on October 20, 1548, the city embodies its founding principles through its official motto: "The dissenters in harmony gathered together in peace and love, and a town of peace they founded, for perpetual memory." Situated at an impressive elevation of 3,639.9216 meters above sea level, La Paz operates in the UTC−4 time zone with a UTC offset of −4. The city covers a total area of 472.0 square kilometers, while its urban area extends to 3,240,000,000.0 square meters. With a total population of 766,468 residents, La Paz maintains a population density of 1,861.24 people per square kilometer, and the metropolitan area encompasses 2,187,223 inhabitants. The city's postal code system ranges from 0201-0220, and it uses area code 2 for telecommunications. La Paz functions as an executive government type. The city hosts numerous significant institutions and landmarks. The Basilica of San Francisco, the Peasant Research and Promotion Center, and Estadio Hernando Siles are all located within La Paz. Educational institutions include the Bolivian Catholic University San Pablo and Universidad Nuestra Señora de La Paz, both maintaining campuses and operations in the city. Casa Grande del Pueblo also calls La Paz home. La Paz has been the site of important historical events, including the 1936 Bolivian coup d'état and the Cuzco Rebellion of 1814. The city has produced notable figures such as Carlos Iturralde Ballivián, footballer Carlos Mendoza, and Carlos Mesa, all of whom were born there. It has also been the final resting place for several prominent individuals, including Carola Cobo, Bartolina Sisa, and Belisario Salinas, while Julia Elena Fortún maintained her residence in the city. The city's cultural and media landscape includes several newspapers with headquarters in La Paz: Cambio, Página Siete, and Bolivia.
