Manama serves as the capital city of Bahrain and holds the distinction of being the country's largest city as well. This important urban center covers a total area of 30.0 square kilometers and maintains a population density of 5,200 people per square kilometer. The city's postal code system uses the format 3XX–4XX for addressing purposes. As Bahrain's capital, Manama has historically served as the administrative center for various political entities, including the former Persian Gulf Residency and the State of Bahrain. The city hosts numerous significant institutions and organizations that reflect its importance as a regional hub. Several government bodies maintain their headquarters there, including the Quality Assurance Authority for Education and Training and the Ministry of Health of Bahrain, both of which also have their primary locations in the city. The educational landscape of Manama includes several notable institutions. The Arabian Gulf University and the College of Health and Sport Sciences are both situated in the city, contributing to its role as an educational center. Additionally, Beit Al Quran, a significant cultural and religious institution, is located in Manama. Manama has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Sami Al-Husaini, Sayed Baqer, and Sayed Shubbar Alawi. The city has also served as the final resting place for various prominent figures, including Saïd bin Saïd Tabbara, Mehnaz Begum, and was the location of the death of Abdulredha Buhmaid. The city's military significance is evident through the presence of several armed forces units. The Royal Bahraini Army, Royal Guard of Bahrain, and Destroyer Squadron 50 all maintain garrisons in Manama. The sports scene is represented by multiple football clubs that use Manama as their home ground, including Al-Ahli Club, Al-Najma SC, and Al-Shabab Club. Various business and media organizations have established their presence in the city. GFH Financial Group has its location in Manama, while the Fakhro Group serves the Manama region. OSN News operates from the city, with Manama listed as both its country and location country. The Progressive Democratic Tribune maintains its headquarters there, and architect Michael David Kirchmann has created significant buildings in the city. Manama also hosted the 2021 Asian Youth Para Games, demonstrating its capacity for international sporting events. Notable residents include Houda Nonoo, who maintains her residence in the city, further emphasizing Manama's role as home to influential figures in the region.
Manila, the capital of the Philippines, is a significant urban center founded on June 24, 1571. The city encompasses a total area of 42.34 square kilometers, while its urban area extends to 1,873,000,000 square meters and its metropolitan area covers 619,570,000 square meters. The metropolitan region is home to 13,484,482 residents. The city operates in the Philippine Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +8. Manila's postal code system ranges from +900 to 1-096. Residents of Manila are known by various demonyms depending on the language: in English, they are called Manileño or Manilan; in Spanish, manilense or manileño(-a); and in Filipino, Manileño(-a), Manilenyo(-a), or Taga-Maynila. Manila embraces two official mottos that reflect its character: "Manila, God First" and "Welcome Po Kayo sa Maynila." The city serves as both a major Philippine city and the nation's capital, housing important government institutions including the Cabinet of the Philippines. Several notable locations are situated within Manila, including Calle Siete, the Capitan Luis Gonzaga Building, and various historically significant sites. The city has been the setting for multiple important battles throughout history, including the Battle of Bangkusay, the Battle of Manila in 1574, and the Battle of Manila in 1762. Manila has served as the birthplace for several notable individuals, including Camille Prats, Carding Castro, and Carl Benito. The city has also been the final resting place for various prominent figures, including Cachupoy, Cal Tjader, and Camilo Osías.
Maputo, a province of Mozambique, serves as the capital and largest city of both modern Mozambique and the former People's Republic of Mozambique, and previously functioned as the capital of Portuguese Mozambique. Founded on December 9, 1876, the city covers a total area of 347.69 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 47 meters above sea level. With a total population of 1,088,449 residents and a metropolitan population of 1,766,823, Maputo operates in the Central Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +2. The city's postal system uses codes ranging from 0101-XX through 0107-XX, while telephone communications follow the area code format (+258) 21-XX-XX-XX. Maputo serves as a significant location for various notable landmarks and institutions, including Praça da Independência, Telecomunicações de Moçambique, and Banco Nacional de Investimento. The city has also been home to several important organizations, with FRELIMO, Movitel SA, and Fastjet Mozambique maintaining their headquarters there. Maputo holds particular significance as a birthplace and final resting place for several notable individuals. Calane da Silva, Campira, and Carlos Fumo were all born in the city, while Calane da Silva, Ruth First, and Moses Mabhida all died there. Carlos Filipe Ximenes Belo has established his residence in Maputo, and the musical artist 340ml considers it their hometown. The city has hosted major sporting events, including the 2011 All-Africa Games, and serves as the home ground for several football clubs: Nova Alianca Maputo, Clube Ferroviário de Maputo, and GD Maputo. Educational institutions in Maputo include the Trichardt School for Christian Education and the American International School of Mozambique. Maputo's strategic location is highlighted by its proximity to natural features, with both Maputo Bay and Kosi Bay identifying the city as their nearest urban center. The city also played a role in Operation Beanbag and serves as the operational base for ADB class diesel multiple units, demonstrating its continued importance in both historical and contemporary contexts.
Mbabane serves as the capital of Eswatini and holds significant importance in the nation's political, economic, and educational landscape. The city covers a total area of 81.76 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 1,243 meters above sea level. With a population of 94,874 residents, Mbabane operates under the postal code H100. The city houses several important government institutions, including the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation of Eswatini, which maintains both its location and headquarters there. The financial sector is represented by Eswatini Bank, which is also located in the capital. Additionally, Royal Swazi National Airways has established its headquarters in Mbabane. Mbabane's educational infrastructure includes multiple institutions of higher learning. Limkokwing University of Creative Technology operates a campus in the city, while Rutherford University and St Mark's School are both situated there as well. The city also serves as home to various religious institutions, including the Mater Dolorosa Church. Several notable individuals were born in Mbabane, including Dennis Masina, Veronica Sentongo, and David Gresham. The city's role as the capital extends beyond contemporary Eswatini, as it has maintained this status throughout the History of Eswatini, reflecting its enduring significance in the nation's development and governance.
Melbourne, located in Australia, is a major city with a total population of 4,917,750. The city serves as the location for several notable institutions and events, including Camberwell Girls Grammar School, the television series Carla Cametti PD, and the Begonia Belle Stakes horse race. Melbourne has been the birthplace of several prominent individuals, including Caitlin Friend, Caitlin Stasey, and Callum Porter. The city has also been the final resting place for notable figures such as Carl Beal, Caroline Hodgson, and Robert Nettleton, all of whom died in Melbourne.
Mexico City, the capital city and megacity of Mexico, stands as one of the world's most significant urban centers. Founded on March 13, 1325, the city has dual founding origins attributed to both Tenoch and Hernán Cortés, reflecting its complex historical heritage. Known by the motto "The City of Palaces," Mexico City encompasses a total area of 1,485 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 2,240 meters above sea level. The metropolis is home to a population of 9,209,944 residents, making it one of the most populous cities in the Americas. The city operates within the Central Time Zone and observes Central Daylight Time, with UTC offsets of −06:00 and −05:00 respectively. Residents and businesses use postal codes ranging from 00 to 16, while the area codes 55 and 56 serve the telecommunications needs of the city. Mexico City has been the birthplace of numerous notable figures, including Camerina Pavón y Oviedo, Camila Sodi, and Cancerbero. The city has also served as the final resting place for several prominent individuals, with Camerina Pavón y Oviedo, Cantinflas, and Caridad Bravo Adams all having died there. The city's infrastructure includes modern transportation systems such as Cablebús, while telecommunications services are provided by companies like Cablemás. Historic streets like Calle de República de Argentina contribute to the urban landscape that has witnessed significant historical events. Throughout its history, Mexico City has been the site of major military conflicts, including the Battle for Mexico City, the Battle of Chapultepec, and the Capture of Mexico City in 1863, events that have shaped both the city's character and Mexico's national history.
Mogadishu, the capital city of Somalia, operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3. Residents of this important urban center are known as Mogadishawi or Hamarawi. The city has served as the capital for multiple political entities throughout history, including the current Transitional Federal Government of Somalia, the former Trust Territory of Somaliland, and the historical Hiraab Imamate. The city houses several key government institutions, with the Ministry of Health, Ministry of Human Rights, and Ministry of Internal Security all maintaining their locations and headquarters in Mogadishu. The educational landscape includes multiple universities, with Benadir University, Baresan University, and the University of Somalia all situated in the city, while Baresan University and Mogadishu University specifically maintain their campuses there. Mogadishu has been the site of significant military conflicts, including the Battle of Deynile and two separate Battles of Mogadishu in 1993 and 2006. The city maintains military significance as the garrison location for the Royal Corps of Somali Colonial Troops, Somali Air Force, and Somali Navy. Several notable individuals have connections to Mogadishu through birth, death, or residence. The city served as the birthplace for athletes Samia Yusuf Omar and Musse Olol, as well as actor Barkhad Abdi. Conversely, it was the place of death for Qamar Aden Ali, Almaas Elman, and Valerie Place. Current residents include Salah Jama, Mahdi Mohammed Gulaid, and Fatiha Serour, while Abukar Umar Adani claims both Mogadishu as his state of origin and nationality. The city's cultural and economic activities are diverse, with the Dur-Dur Band calling it their hometown and Abdulkadir Yahya Ali producing notable work there. Sports teams including Savana FC, Dekedaha FC, and Elman FC use Mogadishu as their ground. Business enterprises such as Premier Bank and Royal Banana Monopoly have established their operations in the city, while the Qaransoor Party maintains its headquarters there. Healthcare infrastructure includes Banadir Hospital, which operates in the Mogadishu region. Transportation connections include Freedom Airline Express, which targets Mogadishu as an airport destination. Interestingly, the data indicates Sub-Saharan Africa lists Mogadishu as a country, representing the city's significant regional importance.
Montevideo serves as the capital city of Uruguay and was founded by Bruno Mauricio de Zabala. The city operates under a mayor-council government system and has adopted the motto "Con libertad ni ofendo ni temo," which translates to "With liberty I offend not, I fear not." Geographically, Montevideo covers a total area of 200.72407855104 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 43.0 meters above sea level. The metropolitan area encompasses a much larger territory of 1639462473.842688 square kilometers. The city maintains a population density of 6726.28570396795 people per square kilometer, while the metropolitan area houses 1947604 residents. For communication and administrative purposes, Montevideo uses the area code (+598) 2XXX XXXX and postal codes in the format 11#00 & 12#00. The city operates in the Uruguay Time zone with a UTC offset of −3. Montevideo has been the location for numerous significant events and institutions. The city houses the Carnival Museum and the Punta Brava Lighthouse. It served as the venue for the 2009 Copa Petrobras Montevideo and was the site of several historic battles, including the Battle of Cerrito, the Battle of Montevideo in 1807, and the Battle of Montevideo in 1823. The city has been home to many notable individuals throughout its history. Camila Colombo, Camila Rajchman, and Camilo Cándido were all born in Montevideo, while Carla Witte, Carlos Aguilera (the theater director), and Carlos Cat all passed away in the city, marking Montevideo as their final resting place.
Montreal is a major Canadian city that was founded on May 17, 1642, and operates under the motto "Concordia Salus," meaning "well-being through harmony." The city is governed by the Montreal City Council and is classified among the list of cities in Quebec. Geographically, Montreal covers a total area of 431.5 square kilometers, with its land area spanning 365,130,000 square meters. The urban area extends across 1,293,990,000 square meters, while the broader metropolitan area encompasses 4,604,260,000 square meters. The city maintains a population of 1,762,949 residents, resulting in a population density of 4,828.3 people per square kilometer. The metropolitan area houses 4,291,732 inhabitants with a density of 919.0 people per square kilometer. Montreal operates within the Eastern Time Zone and observes UTC offsets of −05:00 and −04:00 depending on the season. The city's telecommunications are served by area codes 514, 438, and 263, while postal services utilize codes ranging from H1A through various sequences including H1C-H3N, H3S-H3W, H4A-H4T, H4Z-H5B, H8R-H8Z, H9C-H9E, H9H, and H9K. Residents of Montreal are known by the demonyms Montrealer or Montréalais(e). The city has served as a significant location for various historical events and contemporary activities. Military engagements including the Battle of Longue-Pointe, the Battle of the Cedars, and the Montreal Campaign took place there. Montreal has also been the birthplace of notable individuals such as Cairine Wilson, Caitlin Rother, and Cal Brunker, while serving as the final resting place for figures including Camille Côté, Camillien Houde, and Candide Rochefort. In terms of modern cultural and commercial presence, Montreal serves as the location for the television series "Can You Hear Me?" from 2018, houses the Canada Life Building, and is home to Canada Steamship Lines, demonstrating its continued relevance as a center for media, architecture, and maritime commerce.
Moscow, the capital city of Russia and one of the country's federal cities, serves as a major metropolitan center with a total population of 13,010,112 residents. The city's metropolitan area extends to encompass 20,004,462 people across its broader urban region. Covering a total area of 2,561.498241122304 square kilometers, Moscow maintains a population density of 5,080.09 people per square kilometer. The city sits at an elevation of 156.0 meters above sea level and operates in the Moscow Time zone with a UTC offset of +3. Residents of the city are known as Muscovites, and the municipal government is administered by the Moscow City Duma. The official anthem of Moscow is "Moya Moskva." The city has served as the location for numerous significant places and establishments. Begushchy Kosar, Povarskaya Street, and the President Hotel are all situated within Moscow's boundaries. The city has also been the site of several important historical events, including the Battle of Molodi, the Battle of Moscow in 1612, and the 1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt. Moscow has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Camilla Kolchinsky, Pyotr Albedinsky, and Pyotr Bessonov. The city has also served as the final resting place for various historical figures, with Carl Gustaf Roos, Pranas Eidukevičius, and Prokopy Zubarev all having died in Moscow.
Multan is a city district in Pakistan that operates under the City Districts of Pakistan government type. The city covers a total area of 3,721 square kilometers, while its metropolitan area spans an impressive 560,000,000 square meters. With a total population of 1,871,843 residents, Multan uses the area code 061 and postal codes beginning with 60xxx. The city observes Pakistan Standard Time and maintains a UTC offset of +05:00. Throughout history, Multan has served as the capital for several significant political entities, including the Emirate of Multan, the Lodi dynasty of Multan, and the Langah Sultanate. The city has witnessed important military events, including the Siege of Multan and the Siege of Multan in 1818. Various military forces have maintained garrisons in Multan, including the Sikh Khalsa Army, Fauj-i-Ain, and Fauj-i-Khas. Multan is home to numerous notable landmarks and institutions. The historic Rukn-e-Alam mausoleum is located in the city, as is the Bloody Bastion. Educational institutions with connections to Multan include Bahauddin Zakariya University, which has a campus there, along with Emerson University and Muhammad Nawaz Sharif University of Engineering & Technology. The Board of Intermediate and Secondary Education, Multan is both located in and headquartered in the city. Transportation infrastructure includes Multan International Airport, which serves the city. Several organizations have established their headquarters in Multan, including the Multan Electric Power Company and Aalmi Majlis Tahaffuz Khatm-e-Nubuwwat. The Southern Punjab cricket team uses Multan as their ground, while Nishtar Hospital operates in the region. The city is also the origin of Chaunsa, a variety of mango. Multan has connections to many notable individuals throughout history. Rukn-e-Alam, Robin Kreyer, and Sania Khan were all born in the city, while Aamir Saleem considers it his hometown. The city has also been the final resting place for several prominent figures, including Qandeel Baloch, Bhai Nand Lal, and Rashid Rehman. Diwan Sawan Mal Chopra is known for his association with Multan, and Rana Asif Saeed maintains his residence there.
Mumbai is a megacity located in India, serving as home to a total population of 12,478,447 residents within the city proper and 18,414,288 people across its metropolitan area. The city covers a total area of 603.4 square kilometers, while its metropolitan region spans an impressive 4,355,000,000 square meters. Situated at an elevation of 14 meters above sea level, Mumbai operates under the Indian Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +5:30. The city's residents are known by several demonyms, including Mumbaikar, Bombayite, and Mumbaiite. Mumbai's postal system uses codes ranging from 400 001 to 400 107, and the area code for telephone services is +91-22. The municipal governance of the city falls under the Brihanmumbai Municipal Corporation, which operates as part of India's Municipal Corporations system of government. Mumbai serves as a significant business and cultural center, hosting the locations of several notable companies and organizations. Cadbury, Captain House, and CarTrade.com all maintain their operations in the city. The city has also been the setting for significant historical events, including the 1991 Lokhandwala Complex shootout. As a birthplace, Mumbai has produced several notable individuals, including Candice Pinto, Carlos Cordeiro, and Amit Mistry. The city has also served as the final resting place for various prominent figures, with Amit Mistry, Prabhakar Barwe, and Prabodhankar Thackeray all having died in Mumbai.
Muscat, Oman serves as the capital of Oman and stands as a significant urban center with diverse cultural, educational, and sporting facilities. The city houses several important venues, including the Royal Oman Police Stadium and the Oman Oil and Gas Exhibition Centre, alongside cultural institutions such as the Oman Children's Museum. Educational establishments like Bangladesh School Muscat and Majan College (University College) are situated within the city, contributing to its academic landscape. The city has been the birthplace of notable individuals including Sami Al-Hassawi, Sarah-Jane Dias, and Sayyid Badr Albusaidi, the latter of whom also maintains his residence there. Fatma Al-Nabhani similarly resides in Muscat. Conversely, the city has served as the final resting place for several figures, including Valpy French, Zohurul Hoque, and Natiq Hashim. Muscat's sporting culture is represented through various clubs and teams. Bosher Club, Muscat Club, and Ahli Sidab Club all have their grounds located in the city, while the Oman national under-23 football team uses the city as their stadium base. The city has hosted significant sporting events, including the 2010 Asian Beach Games and the 2012 Oman Super Cup. The business and governmental sectors are well-represented in Muscat, with SalamAir maintaining its headquarters there alongside government ministries including the Ministry of Agriculture and Fisheries Wealth and the Ministry of Civil Service. The luxury perfume company Amouage has established its location in the city as well. Historically, Muscat has been the site of significant events, including the Capture of Muscat in 1552 and Operation Dawn 8: Gulf of Aden. The city's linguistic diversity is reflected in the presence of the Luwati language, which is spoken within its boundaries. Additionally, Qurum is classified as a type within Muscat, contributing to the city's geographical and administrative structure.
N'Djamena, the capital city of Chad, serves as the nation's political and administrative center. The city covers a total area of 104.0 square kilometers and has an elevation of 298.0 meters above sea level. With a total population of 916,000 residents, N'Djamena maintains a population density of 9,148.0 people per square kilometer. The metropolitan area extends significantly beyond the city limits, encompassing 166,000,000.0 square meters and housing a metropolitan population of 1,605,696 inhabitants. The city operates under area code 235 for telecommunications. N'Djamena holds considerable historical and political significance, having served as the capital not only of modern Chad but also of the former French Chad. Additionally, it functions as the capital of the Chari-Baguirmi prefecture. The city has witnessed several major historical events, including the Battle of N'Djamena in 1979, another Battle of N'Djamena in 2008, and the 1990 Chadian coup d'état. The city is home to numerous important institutions and facilities. The University of N'Djamena maintains both its campus and administrative offices within the city. Educational institutions include the Lycée Montaigne de N'Djamena, while sports facilities are represented by the Stade Omnisports Idriss Mahamat Ouya. The N'Djamena Amea Solar Power Station provides energy infrastructure for the region. Several notable individuals have connections to N'Djamena through birth or death. Robert Lokossimbayé, Rodrigue N'Doram, and Roméo Otodjibaye were all born in the city, while Bintou Malloum, François Tombalbaye, and Lol Mahamat Choua died there. The city supports various organizations and enterprises. Military presence includes the Multinational Joint Task Force, which maintains a garrison in N'Djamena. The sports scene features several football clubs that use the city as their home ground, including Postel 2000 FC, Gazelle FC, and Foullah Edifice FC. Aviation and business sectors are represented by companies headquartered in N'Djamena, including Toumaï Air Tchad, Miss Chad, and Mid Express Tchad.
Nagpur is a metropolis located in India, founded by Bakht Buland Shah and operating under a mayor-council government system. The city covers a total area of 393.5 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 310.0 meters above sea level. With a total population of 2,405,665 and a metropolitan population of 2,497,870, Nagpur maintains a population density of 11,000.0 people per square kilometer. Residents of the city are known as Nagpurkar or Nagpurians. The city operates in the Indian Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +5:30. Nagpur's postal codes range from 440 001 to 440 037, and the area code is +91-712. The Nagpur Municipal Corporation serves as part of the city's administrative structure. Nagpur holds significant historical importance, having served as the capital of both the Nagpur kingdom and Central Provinces and Berar. The city was also the site of the Siege of Nagpur, marking its strategic military significance throughout history. Several notable landmarks and institutions are located within Nagpur. Deekshabhoomi, Gorewada Lake, and Namantar Shahid Smarak are all situated in the city. The educational landscape includes numerous prestigious institutions with campuses or locations in Nagpur: G.H.Raisoni Institute of Information Technology, G.H. Raisoni Department of Microbiology and Biotechnology, National Academy of Direct Taxes, Priyadarshini College of Engineering, Cummins College of Engineering for Women, and Visvesvaraya National Institute of Technology Nagpur. The city serves as headquarters for several organizations, including Samata Sainik Dal, National Council of Churches in India, and Bolshevik Party of India. Additionally, Maintenance Command maintains a garrison in Nagpur. Various companies have established their presence in the city, with Maharashtra Metro Rail Corporation Limited and Yantra India having their location city as Nagpur, while Nagpur Mahanagar Parivahan Limited serves the region. Nagpur's natural surroundings include several wildlife sanctuaries, with Umred Pauni Karhandla Wildlife Sanctuary, Gorewada Lake, and Koka Wildlife Sanctuary all having Nagpur as their nearest city. The city has been home to numerous notable individuals throughout history. Several prominent figures were born in Nagpur, including Pramod Sadasheo Moharir, Pravin Datke, and Prem Dhiraal. Others, such as Uttamrao Deorao Patil, Vikram Marwah, and Vitthal Umap, died in the city. Many distinguished personalities have called Nagpur their hometown, including Priyanka Khedkar, Ulhas Kashalkar, and Vidyadhar Vyas, while others like Vasant Sathe, Vijay J. Darda, and Girish Vyas have maintained residences there. Educational connections to the city extend to various individuals, with Gangadhar Pantawane, Wasudev Waman Patankar, and Sonu Sood having received their education in Nagpur. The city also features in architectural history through Sheo Dan Mal's significant building projects, and in sports through the Nagpur Orangers, who use Nagpur as their stadium location.
Nairobi, the capital and largest city of Kenya, serves as a major urban center in East Africa with a total population of 4,397,073 and a metropolitan population of 10,400,676. The city covers an area of 696.1 square kilometers, resulting in a population density of 6,317.6 people per square kilometer. Located at an elevation of 1,676.4 meters, Nairobi operates in the East Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +3, and residents are known as Nairobians. The city uses the area code 020 and is governed by Nairobi County. Nairobi has served as a capital throughout Kenya's political evolution, functioning as the capital of the East Africa Protectorate, Kenya from 1963-1964, and modern Kenya. The city holds significant historical importance, with architect Herbert Baker having designed significant buildings there. The city serves as a major transportation hub, with several airlines operating services to and from Nairobi. DHL International Aviation ME, Skyward Express, and Silverstone Air all use Nairobi as a target airport, while Blue Sky Aviation Services maintains it as a hub airport. The automotive industry also has a presence in the city, with assembly operations for the Fiat 1100, Škoda Fabia Mk1 6Y, and Suzuki Fronte CB71. Nairobi's educational landscape includes several prominent institutions. Aga Khan University and Aljamea-tus-Saifiyah both maintain campuses in the city, while Amref International University and Rosslyn Academy are based there. Braeburn Schools and Brookhouse School operate in the region, and the city has served as an educational destination for individuals like Catherine Samali Kavuma and Attiya Waris. The city has produced notable individuals across various fields. Amina Abdi Rabar, Benjamin Onyango, and Potash Charles Matathia were all born in Nairobi, while Pritam Singh Sandhu, Ruhila Adatia-Sood, and Santokh Singh Matharu died there. Gillian Condy holds Nairobi citizenship, and several prominent figures maintain residences in the city, including Beatrice Elachi, David Maraga, and Davy Kiprotich Koech. Nairobi's cultural scene includes musical groups such as Camp Mulla, Sanaipei Tande, and Sauti Sol, who call the city their hometown. The literary publication Enkare Review is also based in Nairobi. The city serves as headquarters for various organizations and political entities. The Roots Party Kenya, Ministry of Health of Kenya, and Beyond Zero all maintain their headquarters there. Several businesses have established their operations in Nairobi, including Davis & Shirtliff and Cytonn Investments, while MUDI Africa serves the Nairobi region. Military presence in the city includes garrisons for the 7 Kenya Rifles, East Africa Command, and Kenya Air Force. Sports facilities support local football clubs, with Mathare Youth F.C., Gor Mahia F.C., and Ligi Ndogo S.C. all having grounds in Nairobi. The city also serves as a stadium location for the Kenya national under-20 football team and Kenya women's national football team. Healthcare and educational institutions include Nairobi Women's Hospital and Aga Khan University Hospital, both located in the Nairobi region. The city's proximity to natural attractions is notable, with Nairobi National Park, Shompole Conservancy, and Amboseli National Park all having Nairobi as their nearest city. Various organizations maintain locations or connections to Nairobi, including Amici del Mondo World Friends Onlus, Amu Power Company, and Pray & Prey, all of which are located in the city.
Nassau, the capital city of The Bahamas, covers a total area of 207.0 square kilometers and has a population of 274,400 residents. The city operates under area code 242 and is situated in the Eastern Time Zone, with UTC offsets of −5 and −4 depending on daylight saving time. This historic capital has been the site of numerous significant events throughout its history. The city witnessed the Capture of the Bahamas in both 1782 and 1783, as well as the famous Raid of Nassau. Nassau also served as the capital of the Republic of Pirates during its colorful maritime past. The city serves as a major hub for various organizations and institutions. The Progressive Liberal Party, the North American, Central American and Caribbean Athletic Association, and SkyBahamas Airlines all maintain their headquarters in Nassau. Additionally, Castle Bank & Trust (Bahamas) operates from the city, while Lynden Pindling International Airport and radio stations ZNBB-FM and ZNBN-FM are based there. Nassau's sporting landscape includes several football clubs that call the city their home ground, including Bears FC, United F.C., and Dynamos FC. The Roscow A. L. Davies Soccer Field is located within the city. Nassau has also hosted tennis tournaments, including The Bahamas Women's Open in both 2011 and 2012. The city has been home to notable individuals throughout history. Calvin Lockhart, Cameron Hepple, and Rosanna Carter were all born in Nassau, while Roland Robinson, 1st Baron Martonmere, Rosita Butterfield, and Royal Little passed away there. Several contemporary figures maintain residences in Nassau, including tennis players Denis Shapovalov, Eugenie Bouchard, and Nick Kyrgios. Nassau's cultural connections extend to the music industry, with bands T-Connection and The Beginning of the End calling it their hometown, along with musician Rik Carey. The city has served as a recording location for several notable songs, including "Calling America," "Pull Up to the Bumper," and "Satellite 15... The Final Frontier." The city's proximity to natural attractions is evident in its relationship to several national parks and reserves. Blue Holes National Park, Bonefish Pond National Park, and Crab Replenishment Reserve all list Nassau as their nearest city. Additionally, the SS Samingoy operated from Nassau, highlighting the city's maritime connections.
Naypyidaw serves as the capital of Myanmar and was designated as the capital by the State Peace and Development Council. This planned city covers a total area of 7,054.37 square kilometers and has a population of 924,608 residents, resulting in a population density of 131.1 people per square kilometer. Located at an elevation of 115.0 meters above sea level, the city operates under Myanmar Standard Time with a UTC offset of +06:30 and uses the area code 067. The city houses numerous important government institutions and facilities. The Presidential Palace is located within Naypyidaw, along with the Pyidaungsu Hluttaw and Pyithu Hluttaw, which are key legislative bodies. The Naypyidaw Development Committee exercises jurisdiction over the city's administration and development. Several government departments and organizations have established their headquarters in Naypyidaw, including the Department of Higher Education, the Union Civil Service Board, and the Union Election Commission. The city also serves as a military center, with the Myanmar Navy and the Office of the Chief of Air Defence maintaining garrisons there. Additionally, Myanma Economic Bank has its location in the city. As a major urban center, Naypyidaw has hosted several significant sporting events, including the 2018 ASEAN University Games, the 2014 ASEAN Para Games, and the 2015 Myanmar National Sports Festival, demonstrating its capacity to accommodate large-scale international and national competitions.
Nicosia serves as the capital city of the Republic of Cyprus, as well as the capitals of Cyprus, Northern Cyprus, and historically British Cyprus. This significant urban center covers a land area of 51,060,000 square meters and sits at an elevation of 220 meters above sea level. The city has a total population of 55,014 residents, who are known by the demonym Nicosian. The city operates within specific time zones and postal systems that reflect its geographic location and administrative structure. Residents and businesses use postal codes ranging from 1010 to 1107, while the area code +357 22 serves the city's telecommunications needs. The city has also been the site of several significant historical events, including the Battle at Nicosia Hospital, the 1 April attacks in Cyprus, and various Cyprus police station attacks, all of which took place in Nicosia, marking important moments in the region's complex political and social history.

The city is also home to several sports facilities and teams, including the Stade Municipale, which serves as a venue for local sporting events. Multiple football clubs have their grounds in Porto-Novo, including Mogas 90 FC, Postel Sport FC, and AS Dragons FC de l'Ouémé, while Elan Sportif is also located in the city. Cultural and historical landmarks add to Porto-Novo's significance, with the Royal Palace standing as an important architectural and historical site within the city. The city serves as a center for political and media activities, housing the headquarters of both the Communist Party of Benin and La Presse Porto-Novienne, a local publication that contributes to the city's role as an information hub in the region.
Prague, the capital city of Czechia, is a major metropolitan center with a total population of 1,275,406 residents, while its broader metropolitan area encompasses 2,709,418 people. The city covers a total area of 496 square kilometers, with its urban area extending across 298,000,000 square meters. Residents of Prague are known as Praguers, and the city carries the distinctive motto "Brussels of the East." The city operates within the Central European Time zone during standard time and Central European Summer Time during daylight saving periods, corresponding to UTC offsets of +1 and +2 respectively. Prague's postal code system ranges from 100 00 to 199 00, serving its various districts and neighborhoods. Prague serves as the location for several notable institutions and landmarks, including the historic Prague Castle and the Prague Integrated Transport system. The city is also home to Praga Rugby, a local sports organization. Throughout its history, Prague has been the site of significant events, including the Prague Uprising of 1848, the Prague uprising, and the Prague offensive. The city has been both a birthplace and final resting place for numerous notable individuals. Among those born in Prague are Camilla Trinchieri, Carl Borivoj Presl, and Carl Ferdinand Cori. The city has also served as the place of death for several prominent figures, including Carl Borivoj Presl, Prince Karl of Auersperg, and Pyotr Vail.
Praia, the capital city of both Cape Verde and Portuguese Cape Verde, is located in Santiago, Cape Verde, and operates in the Cape Verde Time zone. The city covers a total area of 102.6 square kilometers and has a population of 159,050 residents. The city serves as an important political and administrative center, housing the headquarters of several major political organizations including the Democratic and Independent Cape Verdean Union and the Movement for Democracy. The city features several significant landmarks and public spaces, including Praça Alexandre Albuquerque and Praça Luís de Camões. Historically, Praia has been the site of important military engagements, including the Battle of Porto Praya and the Capture of HMS Cyane and HMS Levant. The city has also been significant in the lives of various notable individuals. It served as the birthplace for several footballers, including Cabral, Caló, and Cao, who was born in 1968. Conversely, Praia was the place where poet Pedro Cardoso died, along with Codé di Dona and Tuna Mascarenhas. The musical group Os Tubarões considers Praia their hometown, further cementing the city's cultural importance in Cape Verde.
Pretoria, the capital city of South Africa, was founded on November 18, 1855, by Marthinus Wessel Pretorius. Located at an elevation of 1,339 meters, Pretoria covers a total area of 687.54 square kilometers, while its metropolitan area spans an impressive 6,297,830,000 square meters. The city has a population of 741,651 residents, with the metropolitan area home to 2,921,488 people. As a metropolitan municipality in South Africa, Pretoria uses the area code 012 and postal code 0001. The city operates in the South African Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +2. Pretoria has served as the capital for multiple political entities throughout history, including the current South Africa, the former Union of South Africa, and the Transvaal Colony. The city is linguistically diverse, with both Gayle language and Pretoria Sotho spoken within its boundaries. The city also serves as the nearest urban center to several natural attractions, including Roodeplaat Nature Reserve, Magaliesberg Biosphere Reserve, and Struben Dam Bird Sanctuary, making it a gateway to the region's natural heritage.

It currently stands as the largest city in the Philippines and was also the largest city during the Fourth Philippine Republic. As a municipality, Rotterdam appears on both the list of cities in the Netherlands by province and the list of municipalities of the Netherlands. Several notable locations are situated within Rotterdam, including Rotown, Rotterdam City Hall, and the Rotterdam Metro system. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, particularly the Battle of Rotterdam and the German bombing of Rotterdam during World War II. Rotterdam has served as both a birthplace and final resting place for various notable individuals. Among those born in the city are Carel Polak, Carien Kleibeuker, and Carl Kuntze. The city has also been the place of death for several individuals, including Puck Oversloot, Puck van Heel, and Robert MacWard.
Salvador, Bahia is a municipality in Brazil that was founded on March 29, 1549. The city serves as an important historical and cultural center, having functioned as the capital of the State of Brazil, Colonial Brazil, and the Governorate General of Bahia. Located at an elevation of 8 meters above sea level, Salvador operates in the Time in Brazil time zone with a UTC offset of minus 3 hours. The city covers a total area of 693 square kilometers, with water areas comprising 66,910,000 square meters of this territory. Salvador's metropolitan area spans an impressive 4,375,123,000 square meters. The municipality has a total population of 2,886,698 residents, resulting in a population density of 4,187 people per square kilometer. The broader metropolitan area houses 3,919,864 inhabitants with a metropolitan population density of 891.3 people per square kilometer. Salvador's residents are known by the demonym Soteropolitano in Portuguese and Soteropolitan in English. The city's postal codes range from 40000-001 to 42599-999, and its area code is +55 71. The municipal motto, expressed in Latin as "Sic illa ad arcam reversa est," translates to "So she returned to the ark" in English. The city holds significant geographical importance, with the Atlantic Ocean, Bay of All Saints, and Baía do Iguape Marine Extractive Reserve all having Salvador as their nearest city. Several notable structures and institutions are located within Salvador, including the Barra Lighthouse, Caramuru Building, Casa Nobre de Jequitaia, and Queimado Fountain. The city also houses the Salvador Air Force Base and serves as the location for Vai Anitta. Salvador has been the site of several important historical events, including the Capture of Salvador, the Malê revolt, and the Siege of Salvador in 1638. The city has strong connections to Brazilian football, serving as the ground for Botafogo Sport Club and Sport Club Santos Dumont, while also hosting the headquarters of the Federação Bahiana de Futebol. Additionally, Abaeté Aviação maintains its headquarters in the city. The municipality has been home to numerous notable figures throughout its history. Several footballers were born in Salvador, including Cabinho, Cabore, and Cadu, who was born in 1997. The city has also been the final resting place for prominent individuals such as Carybé, Castro Alves, and Rodolfo Bottino. Salvador holds particular significance for Manuel da Nóbrega, who is known for his association with the city. The cultural landscape of Salvador is enriched by its connection to various musical groups and artists who call it their hometown, including Pepeu Gomes, Novos Baianos, and Banda Eva, contributing to the city's vibrant artistic heritage and cultural identity within Brazil.
San José, Costa Rica serves as the capital city of Costa Rica, the Free State of Costa Rica, and is recognized as the capital in the context of human rights in Costa Rica. Founded on May 16, 1823, the city operates under the motto "Towards better things" or "Ad Meliora" in Latin. Located at an elevation of 1,172 meters, San José covers a total area of 44.62 square kilometers and has a population of 342,188 residents. The metropolitan area encompasses a significantly larger region, spanning 2,044,000,000 square meters with a metropolitan population of 2,158,898 people, resulting in a population density of 1,056.2 people per unit area. The city operates in the Central Time Zone with a UTC offset of -6 hours and uses the area code +506. San José serves as a significant cultural and institutional hub, housing notable establishments such as the Pre-Columbian Gold Museum, the United World College of Costa Rica, and Universidad Cristiana del Sur. The city has hosted major events including the 2011 Seguros Bolívar Open San José, the 2013 Central American Games, and the 2002 San José mayoral election. Juan Santamaría International Airport is located in the city, serving as a hub for Air Costa Rica. The city has been the birthplace of several notable figures, including Carlos Alvarado Quesada, Carlos Avendaño Calvo, and Carlos Echandi. It has also been the place of death for Carlos José Solórzano, Carlos Soley, and Carlos Toppings. Currently, several prominent individuals maintain residence in San José, including Josette Altmann Borbón, Leila Rodríguez Stahl, and Lorena Clare Facio. San José's industrial significance is demonstrated through its role as an assembly location for vehicles including the AMC Hornet and AMC Matador. The city serves as headquarters for various organizations such as the Peliquista Party, Reinas de Costa Rica, and Costa Rica Green Airways, while also being the location city for Banco de Costa Rica. The area's sporting culture is represented by several teams that call San José their home ground, including Sociedad Gimnástica Española de San José, A.D. Sagrada Familia, and Sporting F.C. Additionally, the city serves as the hometown for musical groups and individuals such as Escats, Luis Montalbert-Smith, and Sintagma. San José's proximity to natural attractions is highlighted by its position as the nearest city to both Braulio Carrillo National Park and Juan Castro Blanco National Park, making it an important gateway to Costa Rica's natural heritage.
Santa Cruz de la Sierra is a municipality in Bolivia that holds the distinction of being the country's largest city. Founded on February 26, 1561, this significant urban center has grown to encompass a total area of 1,345 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 400 meters above sea level. The metropolitan area is home to a substantial population of 2,424,120 residents, making it a major demographic hub within Bolivia. The city operates within the UTC−4 time zone, maintaining a UTC offset of −4 hours, and uses the area code (+591) 3 for telecommunications. Santa Cruz de la Sierra serves as an important transportation center, hosting both Viru Viru International Airport and El Trompillo Airport within its boundaries. The city's sporting infrastructure includes two notable stadiums: Estadio Edgar Peña Gutierrez and Estadio Juan Carlos Durán, which serve the local community's athletic needs. Several prominent individuals have connections to Santa Cruz de la Sierra through birth or death. The city served as the birthplace for racquetball player Carlos Keller, footballer Carlos Lampe, and Carlos Melchor Díaz. Conversely, it was the place where José Miguel de Velasco, Juan Pereda, and Paul Burton passed away, marking significant moments in their respective lives. The city has played host to major sporting events, including the 1993 Bolivarian Games, demonstrating its capacity for international competition. Educational opportunities are provided by Gabriel René Moreno Autonomous University, which is located within the city limits. Santa Cruz de la Sierra also supports various football clubs, with Royal Pari F.C., Club Calleja, and Club Destroyers all maintaining their grounds there. As a commercial center, the city serves as headquarters for several important organizations and companies, including Línea Aérea Amaszonas airline, the Reina Hispanoamericana beauty pageant organization, and Unitel Bolivia broadcasting company. The musical group Azul Azul considers Santa Cruz de la Sierra their hometown, while notable residents include María Fernanda Álvarez Terán and Federico Zeballos, who have chosen to make their residence in this vibrant Bolivian city.
Santiago, Chile serves as a significant hub for numerous organizations, institutions, and individuals across various sectors. The city hosts several prominent companies and organizations, including the television program Calle 7, the gaming company AmnesiaGames, and the healthcare organization Provida, all of which maintain their operations there. Santiago has been the site of important historical events, including the 1925 Chilean coup d'état and two significant military engagements: the Battle of Chacabuco and the Battle of Maipú. These events have contributed to the city's historical significance in Chilean national development. The city has been both a birthplace and final resting place for notable individuals. Camila Zárate Zárate, Camilo Gaínza, and Camilo José Vergara were all born in Santiago, while the city served as the place of death for Camilo Mori, Carlos Giudice, and Carlos González Cruchaga. Additionally, Gaston Orellana received his training in Santiago. Santiago's educational landscape includes several major institutions. Major University maintains a campus in the city, while San Sebastián University and the University of Chile are both located there. The city also houses Santiago Chicureo Airport, providing aviation services to the region. In the realm of sports, Santiago serves as the home ground for Club Deportivo Universidad Católica and Real León. The city functions as headquarters for multiple political organizations, including the Democratic Independent Regionalist Party, Democratic Revolution, and Humanist Action. The music scene in Santiago includes several bands that call the city their hometown, such as Amerindios, Bbs Paranoicos, and Profetas y Frenéticos. The entertainment industry is represented by Cinépolis Chile, which has its location city in Santiago. Santiago also serves as a residential base for various prominent figures, including journalist Beatriz Sánchez, Horacio de la Peña, and José Piñera. The nearby ski resort La Parva considers Santiago its nearest city, highlighting the capital's role as a regional center for both urban activities and recreational access to mountain destinations.
Santo Domingo, the capital city of the Dominican Republic, stands as a historic metropolis founded on August 5, 1496. Known by its motto "Ciudad Primada de América" (First City of America), the city encompasses a total area of 104.44 square kilometers at an elevation of 14 meters above sea level. The metropolitan area spans an impressive 2,696,690,000 square meters, housing a metropolitan population of 2,995,211 residents, while the city proper contains 1,484,789 inhabitants. Residents of Santo Domingo are known as Capitaleño for males and Capitaleña for females. The city operates within the Atlantic Standard Time zone and uses area codes 809, 829, and 849 for telecommunications. Postal services are organized under codes 10100–10699 for the Distrito Nacional. Santo Domingo's strategic location makes it the nearest major city to several important geographical features, including the Caribbean Sea, the American Mediterranean Sea, and Parque Nacional Submarino La Caleta. Throughout history, Santo Domingo has served as the capital for multiple political entities, including the Captaincy General of Santo Domingo, the Columbian Viceroyalty, and España Boba. The city has been the site of numerous significant military engagements, including the Santo Domingo Affair, the Battle of Duarte Bridge, and the Battle of Santo Domingo in 1586. Notable military figures such as Ramón Power y Giralt and François Antoine Charles Lallemand participated in battles at Santo Domingo. The city has been home to various colonial structures documented in the List of colonial buildings in Santo Domingo. Educational institutions have established themselves in the city, including Carol Morgan School and Santo Domingo Institute of Technology. The business sector is represented by companies such as Viva network operator, which maintains its location there, along with the Industrial Development and Competitiveness Center. Santo Domingo has served as the birthplace for several notable individuals, including Camil Domínguez, Carlos Bonilla Sánchez, and baseball player Carlos Contreras. The city has also been the final resting place for Carmen Castillo, Carmen Quidiello, and Rosa Gómez de Mejía. Contemporary residents have included José Hernández-Fernández, José Núñez de Cáceres, and José Olivares, while Carmen Rosa Caso, Prisilla Rivera, and Rosa Medrano call it their hometown. The city's cultural and political landscape includes organizations such as the Blue Party of the Dominican Republic, Dominican Today, and Dominicana de Aviación, all of which maintain their headquarters in Santo Domingo. Sports teams O&M FC and Bob Soccer School FC use the city as their home ground, while the transportation network includes route DR-13 serving the city. The recording industry has also found a place in Santo Domingo, with songs like "La llave de mi corazón" being recorded there. Additionally, the area of Ensanche Espaillat is classified as a Santo Domingo type district.
Sarajevo, the capital city of Bosnia and Herzegovina, is a significant urban center with a total area of 141.5 square kilometers and an elevation of 550 meters above sea level. The city has a total population of 275,524 residents, while its metropolitan area encompasses a much larger population of 555,210 people across an urban area of 419,160,000 square meters and a metropolitan area spanning 3,350,000,000 square meters. The city operates under the postal code 71000 and area code +387 33, functioning in both Central European Time and Central European Summer Time zones with UTC offsets of +1 and +2 respectively. Sarajevo is governed by the Sarajevo City Council. The city holds considerable historical significance, having served as the capital for multiple political entities including the Bosnia Eyalet, Bosnia vilayet, and modern Bosnia and Herzegovina. Several important military engagements took place in Sarajevo, including the Battle of Sarajevo in 1878, the Battle of Vrbanja Bridge, and the Sarajevo Operation. The city has been home to various military units, with the Green Berets Bosnian paramilitary, Patriotic League of Bosnia and Herzegovina, and the 1st Corps of the Army of the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina all maintaining garrisons there. Sarajevo has been the birthplace of notable individuals including Predrag Benaček, Predrag Danilović, and Predrag Finci, while also serving as the final resting place for Beba Selimović, Bogdan Žerajić, and Boris Bračulj. The city continues to be home to several residents including Predrag Kojović, Saša Magazinović, and Bariša Čolak, and Marko Vego is particularly known for his association with the city. The city serves as an important industrial center, having been an assembly location for various Volkswagen models including the Golf Mk1, Jetta A1, and Jetta A2. Sarajevo hosts numerous cultural and educational institutions, including the University of Sarajevo School of Economics and Business, which maintains its campus in the city, and the Sarajevo Graduate School of Business. The Sarajevo International Airport provides air connectivity for the region. Various cultural events and organizations are based in Sarajevo, including the Pravo Ljudski Film Festival and several media outlets such as Behar magazine and Behar TV, both of which operate from the city. The music scene is particularly vibrant, with several bands calling Sarajevo their hometown, including Zabranjeno pušenje band members, Bezbeli Apstraklije, and Bijelo Dugme. The song "Mafia" by Jala Brat and Buba Corelli was recorded in the city. Several businesses and organizations have established their presence in Sarajevo, with companies like Robot, Unioninvest, and M&H Company maintaining their city locations there. Political organizations including the Party of Rights of Bosnia and Herzegovina 1861 and the Bosnian-Herzegovinian Patriotic Party have their headquarters in the city. BIRN Bosnia and Herzegovina serves the Sarajevo region, while the sports club FK Bosna Sarajevo uses the city as its ground. The city is also home to various landmarks and facilities, including the Sarajevo City Center and Sarajevo Disk, both located within the city limits. The nearby Skakavac waterfall is situated close to Sarajevo, making it the nearest city to this natural attraction.
Seoul, the capital city of South Korea, is a major metropolitan area with a total population of 9,443,722 residents spread across 605.21 square kilometers. The city sits at an elevation of 38.0 meters above sea level and proudly displays the motto "I • Seoul • U." As a special city of South Korea, Seoul operates under a mayor-council government system, with governance shared between the Seoul Metropolitan Government and the Seoul Metropolitan Council. The city serves as headquarters for several important national institutions, including the Presidential Council on Nation Branding, Korea, the Presidential Security Service, and Presseum. Seoul's strategic importance is reflected in its history as the site of significant military engagements, including the Battle of Namdaemun, the Battle of Suwon Airfield, and the Blue House raid. Seoul has been the birthplace of numerous notable figures in the entertainment industry, including musicians Primary, Psy, and singer Punch. The city has also been the final resting place for several prominent individuals, serving as the location where Pyon Yong-tae, Roh Hoe-chan, and former president Roh Tae-woo passed away. Through its role as both a governmental center and cultural hub, Seoul continues to be a focal point of South Korean national life and international recognition.
Shanghai is a direct-administered municipality of China with a total population of 24,870,895 and a metropolitan population of 41,354,149. The city covers a total area of 6,341 square kilometers, with its metropolitan area spanning 14,922,700,000 square meters and water areas covering 697,000,000 square meters. Located at an elevation of 4 meters above sea level, Shanghai operates in the China Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +08:00. The municipality uses the area code 21 and postal codes ranging from 200000 to 202100. Residents of Shanghai are known as Shanghainese, reflecting the city's distinct cultural identity. Shanghai serves as the location for several notable facilities and landmarks, including the Power Station of Art, Pudong Football Stadium, and Pudong International Information Port. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, including the Battle of Shanghai, the Battle of Shanghai in 1861, and the Defense of Sihang Warehouse. The municipality has connections to various notable individuals throughout history. Cai Chusheng, Cai Dafeng, and Cai Hesen were all born in Shanghai, while the city served as the place of death for Cao Tianqin, Cao Ying (a translator), and Prosper Bernard.
Sharjah is a metropolis with a total population of 1,274,749 and a metropolitan area spanning 235,500,000 square meters. The city operates under an absolute monarchy form of government and has served as the capital of the Trucial States. The city is home to numerous companies and organizations, including Arada, a company located there, as well as several media entities. Geo Entertainment, Geo News, and Geo Super all maintain their headquarters in Sharjah. Additionally, Dana Gas PJSC has established its location in the city. Sharjah features various notable establishments and infrastructure. Kshisha Park and Al Bait Hotel are both situated within the city. The E 611 road of the United Arab Emirates also runs through Sharjah. Several prominent individuals have connections to the city through birth or death. The city has also been associated with recognition and awards, as evidenced by Wijdan Al-Sayegh receiving an award from Sharjah, highlighting the city's role in honoring achievements and contributions.
Singapore is a city-state and unitary state with a total population of 5,637,000 people and a population density of 7,804.0 per square kilometer. The nation's citizens are known as Singaporeans, and the country operates under the motto "Onward Singapore." The Parliament of Singapore serves as the country's legislature, while the Cabinet of Singapore is located within the nation. Singapore uses the Singapore dollar as its currency and operates in the Singapore Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +8. Singapore recognizes multiple official languages, including English, Malay, and Singaporean Mandarin, with Malay also serving as a general language of the country. The nation's diverse population comprises several ethnic groups, including Chinese Singaporeans and Indian Singaporeans, with the overall ethnic composition detailed in the Demographics of Singapore. Religious diversity characterizes Singapore, with various faiths practiced including Hinduism in Singapore, Islam in Singapore, and irreligion also present among the population. This multicultural and multi-religious society reflects the nation's complex demographic makeup. Several notable individuals have connections to Singapore through birth or death. Calvin Kang Li Loong, Carol Smith (a radio presenter), and Carole Lin were all born in Singapore, while Ami Chandra, Punch Coomaraswamy, and Quah Chin Lai died there. The country has been the site of significant historical events, including the Battle of Bukit Timah, Battle of Kranji, and Battle of Pasir Panjang. Singapore also hosts various locations and events, such as Campus Party and Canberra Plaza, Singapore, demonstrating its role as a hub for both historical significance and contemporary activities.

Located at an elevation of 240 meters, Skopje operates under the postal code МК-10 00 and area code +389 2. Residents of the city are known as Skopjans. The city observes Central European Time and Central European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2 respectively. Skopje has served as a capital for multiple historical entities, including Independent Macedonia in 1944, the Sanjak of Üsküp, and the Tsardom of Bulgaria, reflecting its long-standing political importance in the region. Skopje is home to numerous educational institutions, including South East European University, which has a campus in the city, as well as Josip Broz Tito High School and University American College Skopje. The city also houses several media organizations, with MRT 1, MRT 2, and MRT 3 television channels all maintaining their headquarters there, alongside Metropolis Radio. The city has significant military connections, serving as a garrison for both the VII Corps of the Ottoman Empire and the North Macedonia Air Brigade. In the sports realm, FK Vardar has its ground in Skopje, and the North Macedonia national football team uses the city as their stadium location. Architect Drago Ibler has a significant building in Skopje, and Pasha Yiğit Bey participated in a military service battle there. Sofia's civic identity is reflected in its motto "Ever growing, never aging," which appears in Bulgarian as "Расте, но не старее." The city has been the location of several significant historical events, including the 1923 Bulgarian coup d'état, the Battle of Sofia, and the Siege of Serdica in 809. The city's coastal location is highlighted by its proximity to the Caribbean Sea, for which St. George's serves as the nearest city.

Stockholm, the capital city of Sweden, is a municipality with a total population of 978,770 people within its boundaries and a metropolitan population of 2,415,139. The city covers a total area of 188.0 square kilometers, while its urban area extends to 381,630,000 square meters and the metropolitan area encompasses 6,519,000,000 square meters. Suva, the capital city of Fiji, serves as the nation's political and administrative center with a total area of 26.24 square kilometers and a population of 93,970 residents. The city operates under the governance of the Suva City Council and maintains the motto "Valataka na Dina (Fight for the Right)." Located in the UTC+12 time zone, Suva has held significant historical importance as the capital not only of modern Fiji but also of the former Colony of Fiji and the British Western Pacific Territories. The city houses numerous important government institutions, including the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation of Fiji, which maintains both its location and headquarters there. Several political organizations have established their headquarters in Suva, including the People's Alliance and the Media Industry Development Authority of Fiji. The military presence is represented by the Fiji Infantry Regiment and Counter Revolutionary Warfare Unit, both of which maintain garrisons in the city. Suva's educational landscape includes prominent institutions such as the University of the South Pacific, which has its city campus there, and the Fiji School of Medicine, which operates its campus in the city. The city has also been a significant venue for regional sporting events, hosting both the 1963 and 1979 South Pacific Games. Several notable facilities and organizations call Suva home, including the Royal Suva Yacht Club, Colonial War Memorial Hospital, Paradise Beverages, and HFC Bank Stadium, which the city operates. The surrounding area features natural attractions, with the Colo-i-Suva Forest Reserve, Pacific Ocean, and Sovi Basin all located near the city. Suva has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Carl Probert, Samuela Anise, and Sapeta Taito, while also serving as the final resting place for Savenaca Tamaibeka, Epineri Vula, and Meli Loki. The city continues to be home to various residents, including Makelesi Bulikiobo-Batimala, Banuve Tabakaucoro, and Timoci Tuivaga, and serves as the hometown for others such as Savuto Vakadewavosa, Elena Baravilala, and Daniel Rae Costello. Historically, Suva was also the location where the 2006 Fijian coup d'état took place, marking it as a site of significant political events in the nation's recent history.

Vientiane has played host to numerous significant sporting events, including the 2009 Southeast Asian Games, the 2012 South East Asian Table Tennis Championships, and the 2012 ASEAN University Games. The city is also home to several football clubs, with Master 7 FC, Lao Police Club, and Ezra F.C. all using Vientiane as their ground. Educational institutions are represented by the Vientiane International School, which operates within the city. The city has witnessed important historical events, including the Battle of Vientiane and both the 1960 and 1964 Laotian coups. It has served as a military center, with the Royal Lao Air Force, Royal Lao Army Airborne, and Royal Lao Navy all maintaining garrisons there. The Parliament of the Kingdom of Laos was located in Vientiane, and the city features notable accommodations such as the Royal Dokmaideng Hotel. Several prominent individuals have connections to Vientiane through birth or death. Santisouk Inthavong, Saymanolinh Paseuth, and Saynakhonevieng Phommapanya were all born in the city, while Sali Vongkhamsao, Maichantan Sengmani, and Sisavath Keobounphanh all died there. The regional dish Nam khao is associated with the Vientiane region, reflecting the city's cultural significance.
Warsaw is a city with powiat rights located in Poland, serving as a significant urban center with a rich historical and cultural heritage. The city operates under a mayor-council government system and is governed by the Warsaw City Council. Warsaw's residents are known as Varsovians, and the city proudly bears the Latin motto "Semper invicta," meaning "Ever invincible." Geographically, Warsaw sits at an elevation of 78 meters and covers a total area of 517.24 square kilometers. The city has a population of 1,860,281 people, resulting in a population density of 3,596 people per square kilometer. The broader metropolitan area encompasses 6,100,430,000 square meters and houses 3,100,844 residents, with a metropolitan population density of 509.1 people per square kilometer. Warsaw operates in the Central European Time zone during standard time and Central European Summer Time during daylight saving periods, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2 respectively. The city's postal codes range from 00-001 to 04-999, and its area code is +48 22. The city has been home to numerous notable landmarks and institutions, including the Carmelite Church, Potocki Palace, and Połczyńska Street, all located within Warsaw's boundaries. Historically, Warsaw has been the site of several significant military engagements, including the Battle of Białołęka, the Battle of Nasielsk, and the Battle of Olszynka Grochowska. Warsaw has also been connected to many prominent individuals throughout history. The city served as the birthplace of notable figures such as Casimir Funk, Przemysław Bobak, and Przemysław Czyż. Additionally, several distinguished individuals spent their final days in Warsaw, including Calel Perechodnik, Predrag Đajić, and Przemysław Gintrowski, making the city their place of death.
Washington, D.C. serves as both the capital city and federal district of the United States. The city encompasses a total area of 176.99978746036223 square kilometers, with land covering 158,118,774.1360128 square meters and water areas accounting for 18,881,013.32434944 square meters. With a total population of 689,545 residents, Washington, D.C. maintains a population density of 4,360.931216218876 people per square kilometer, while the broader metropolitan area is home to 6,385,162 inhabitants. Residents of Washington, D.C. are known as Washingtonians, and the city's motto is "Justice for All." The district operates within the Eastern Time Zone, observing UTC offsets of −5 and −4 hours depending on daylight saving time. Communication within the city is facilitated through area codes 202 and 771, with the latter serving as an overlay. The postal system serves the region through zip codes ranging from 20001–20098, 20201–20599, and 56901–56999. Washington, D.C. has served as the location for numerous significant events and institutions. The Cabinet of the United States operates from the city, while historical events such as the Puerto Rican Nationalist Party revolts of the 1950s and the Burning of Washington took place there. The city has also been the setting for various cultural works, including the productions "Cady-Lee" and "Call to Danger." The district has been both a birthplace and final resting place for many notable individuals. Among those born in Washington, D.C. are voice actress Caitlin Glass, columnist Cal Thomas, and football player Caleb Williams. The city has also served as the final resting place for several prominent figures, including demographer Calvin Beale, Calvin Brent, and Calvin Clarke.
Weno serves as a significant hub in the Federated States of Micronesia, holding the distinction of being the country's largest city. The city hosts several important educational institutions, including Chuuk High School and Xavier High School, Micronesia, with the latter also operating St. Xavier Academy within its system. Transportation infrastructure is provided by Chuuk International Airport, which is located in Weno. The city has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including athletes Jack Howard and John Howard, who is specifically known as a Micronesian sprinter, as well as Maria Ikelap. Conversely, Weno also served as the final resting place for Petrus Mailo, who died there. Weno's significance extends beyond education and transportation, as it houses important cultural and historical sites. The Tonotan Guns and Caves are located within the city, adding to its historical importance. Additionally, the city serves as an administrative center, hosting the headquarters of the Chuuk Women's Council, which demonstrates its role in regional governance and community organization.
Windhoek, the capital city of Namibia, serves as a significant political and cultural center in southern Africa. The city was founded on October 18, 1890, and operates under a mayor-council government system. With its motto "Suum Cuique," which is Latin for "To each his own," Windhoek embodies principles of fairness and individual rights. Geographically, Windhoek covers a total area of 5,133 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 1,655 meters above sea level. The city has a population of 431,000 residents, resulting in a population density of 62.8 people per square kilometer. Located in the South African Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +2, Windhoek uses the area code 061 and postal code 10005 for communications and mail services. Windhoek's historical significance extends beyond its current role as Namibia's capital, as it previously served as the capital of German South West Africa and South West Africa. The city hosts numerous important institutions, including the University of Namibia and the School of Military Science, both of which have their campus and city locations in Windhoek. Energy 100 FM, a radio station, also operates from the city. The military presence in Windhoek is substantial, with several units maintaining garrisons there, including the Namibian Special Forces, Signal Regiment, and 21 Motorised Infantry Brigade. Various organizations have established their headquarters in the city, such as the Republican Party, United Democratic Front, and Congress of Democrats. Additionally, the Namibia Nature Foundation, MTC Namibia, and Sanderburg are all located in Windhoek. The city has been home to notable individuals throughout its history. Cameron Klassen, Carmen Bassingthwaighte, and Casper Viviers were all born in Windhoek, while several prominent figures including Rosalia Nghidinwa, Björn von Finckenstein, and Joseph Obgeb Jimmy died there. Current residents include Rosalia Nghidinwa, Bernhardt Esau, and John Mutorwa. Henno Martin is particularly known for his association with Windhoek. Windhoek's cultural landscape includes various entertainment and sports organizations. Musical artists Black Vulcanite, Gal Level, and D-Naff call the city their hometown. The sports scene features several football clubs that use Windhoek as their ground, including Black Africa S.C., Tura Magic F.C., and African Stars F.C. The city's influence extends to nearby attractions, with the Namib-Naukluft National Park identifying Windhoek as its nearest city. Yamoussoukro is a significant city in Ivory Coast, serving as the nation's capital as well as the capital of both the Lacs Region and Crime in Ivory Coast. The city serves as home to several important institutions and landmarks. The Parliament of Ivory Coast is located in Yamoussoukro, along with the renowned Basilica of Our Lady of Peace. Yangon, located in Myanmar, serves as the country's largest city and holds significant historical importance as the former capital of several political entities, including the State of Burma, British rule in Burma, and Post-independence Burma from 1948 to 1962. The State Peace and Development Council also recognized Yangon as its largest city. The city operates under the Myanmar Time zone with a UTC offset of +6:30, and residents are known as Yangonites. Yangon's area code is 01. The metropolitan area of Yangon spans an impressive 10,170,000,000 square meters, while the urban area covers 598,750,000 square meters. The metropolitan population reaches 7,360,703 residents, making it a major population center in the region. Yangon serves as the location for numerous institutions and organizations. The city also houses several healthcare institutions, including East Yangon General Hospital, Yangon Central Women's Hospital, and Yangon ENT Hospital. Business enterprises such as Peace Myanmar Group, Phandeeyar, and City Mart Holdings have established their operations in the city. Additionally, Mizzima News operates from Yangon. The city has been home to numerous notable individuals throughout its history. The city also serves as the hometown for entertainers May Kha Lar, Me N Ma Girls, and Si Thu Lwin. Yangon has played host to various events and productions, including Quest to Million and Operation Dracula. The city features commercial establishments such as Samanea Yangon Market and serves as an assembly location for the Suzuki Cultus Crescent. Historical shipbuilding activities took place in Yangon, with vessels including the Amboyna (1807 ship) and General Baird (1801 ship) constructed there. The city encompasses several townships, including Sanchaung Township and Botataung Township, both classified under Yangon's administrative structure. Natural attractions near the city include Hlawga Park and Kandawgyi Lake. Bank Negara Indonesia extends its services to the Yangon region, reflecting the city's economic significance in the broader regional context.
Yaoundé, the capital city of Cameroon, is a significant urban center with a total area of 180.0 square kilometers and an elevation of 726.0 meters above sea level. The city has a substantial population of 2,765,600 residents and operates in the Central European Time and Central European Summer Time zones, with a UTC offset of +1. As the capital, Yaoundé has served this role not only for modern Cameroon but also historically for French Cameroon and Kamerun. The city also supports a vibrant sports scene, with several football clubs including Diamant Yaoundé, AS Lausanne de Yaoundé, and Tonnerre Yaoundé using the city as their home ground.
